Prophethood
beginner
5 min
The Purpose of Messengers Removes Excuses
Argument: foreknowledge as excuse contradicts messenger purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic argument from sending messengers refutes the idea that God's foreknowledge prevents faith.

Core Idea
God's foreknowledge cannot be an excuse for disbelief.

The author now presents a second scriptural proof, this time focusing on the purpose of sending messengers. The Quran states that messengers were sent so that people would have no excuse against Allah. If God's foreknowledge were a barrier to faith, it would actually provide people with the strongest excuse. This passage examines that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's words and the Quranic verses sink in.
Notice the two distinct Quranic verses quoted.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Find the two verses: 4:165 and 20:134. What common theme do they share? Both emphasize that God removes any excuse people might have.
The key phrase is 'so that mankind will have no argument against Allah after the messengers.'
3
Understand the conditional argument
The author argues: If God's foreknowledge and His announcement of disbelief were a barrier to faith, then that would be a great excuse. But the Quran shows God eliminates all excuses. Therefore, foreknowledge cannot be a barrier.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Draw the conclusion
The conclusion is clear: knowledge of disbelief does not prevent faith. People remain responsible for their choices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إنه تعالى قال : رسلاً مبشرين ومنذرين لئلا يكون للناس على الله : حجة بعد الرسل . وقال : ( ولو أنا أهلكناهم بعذاب من قبله . لقالوا : ربنا لولا أرسلت إلينا رسولاً . فتتبع آياتك من قبل أن نذل ونخزي ) . بين تعالى أنه ما أبقى لهم عذراً، إلا وقد أزاله عنهم . ولو كان علمه بكفرهم، وخبره عن كفرهم : بياناً لهم عن الإيمان، لكان ذلك من أعظم الأعذار، وأقوى الوجوه الدافعة للعقاب عنهم . ولما لم يكن كذلك، علمنا : أن العلم بعدم الإيمان، لا يمنع من الإيمان .
The second: He Almighty said: 'Messengers as bringers of good tidings and warners so that mankind will have no argument against Allah after the messengers' (4:165). And He said: 'And if We had destroyed them with a punishment before him, they would have said: Our Lord, why did You not send to us a messenger so we could have followed Your verses before we were humiliated and disgraced?' (20:134). He Almighty made clear that He did not leave any excuse for them except that He removed it from them. And if His knowledge of their disbelief and His report of their disbelief were a barrier to them from faith, then that would be among the greatest excuses and the strongest factors repelling punishment from them. Since that is not the case, we know that knowledge of non-existence does not prevent from faith.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the second scriptural proof. The author quotes two verses. The first (4:165) states that messengers were sent so that people would have no excuse against God after the messengers. The second (20:134) states that if God had punished people before sending a messenger, they would have complained that they had no warner. The point is that God removes all excuses through messengers. If God's foreknowledge and His announcement that someone will not believe were a barrier to faith, then that would become a powerful excuse for the disbeliever—they could say 'God knew I wouldn't believe, so I am not to blame.' But the Quran shows that such excuses are not valid; rather, people are held accountable. Therefore, knowledge of non-existence does not prevent faith or remove responsibility.

Key Terms
العلم بعدم الإيمان
الخبر عن الكفر
إزالة الأعذار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's foreknowledge gives people an excuse to disbelieve.
Correction: God's foreknowledge does not compel disbelief; it is a knowledge without causative force. The Quran shows that all excuses are removed by sending messengers, so foreknowledge does not provide a valid excuse.

Checkpoint
How does the verse 'so that mankind will have no argument against Allah after the messengers' refute the idea that God's foreknowledge prevents faith?
A) Because if foreknowledge prevented faith, then people would have an argument (excuse) after the messengers, but the verse says they will have no argument.
B) Because the verse says messengers are sent to force people to believe.
C) Because the verse says God's knowledge is irrelevant.
D) Because the verse says messengers are sent only to believers.

Key Takeaway
God's foreknowledge does not remove human responsibility; the purpose of messengers is to eliminate any excuse.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used the fact that 'God knows everything' as a passive excuse for not striving harder in your faith? When faced with this lesson, can you honestly say you will abandon that excuse starting today?
?
If you truly believed that no excuse remains after hearing the truth, what specific habit or sin would you immediately confront in your life that you previously blamed on 'fate' or 'God's will'?
?
Imagine standing before Allah with the argument 'You knew I would disbelieve, so it's not my fault.' This lesson shows that excuse is invalid. What does that mean for the way you respond to divine commands from this moment forward?

The Ninth Proof: Miracles as Divine Acts
The ninth proof challenges Mu'tazila by asking what prevents devils from performing miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument against the Mu'tazilite claim that humans create their own actions, and how it preserves the evidential value of miracles for prophethood.

Core Idea
If anyone can create miracles, even devils, then miracles prove nothing.

This lesson presents a concise but powerful proof from the classical Sunni tradition against the Mu'tazilite position on human agency. The proof uses a simple question to expose a devastating consequence: if humans can be genuine originators of acts, then there is no way to ensure that miracles—the primary evidence for prophethood—are not produced by devils. Thus, the very basis for verifying a prophet's truthfulness would collapse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author directly addresses the Mu'tazila and presents a short, logical argument.
The passage is a single proof, so every word matters.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite premise
Find the premise that the author challenges: 'you permit the servant to be an originator.' This is the Mu'tazilite view that humans create their own acts.
The Arabic term 'mujid' means one who brings something into existence.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
The author then asks: what prevents devils from being the ones who produce miracles? If that is possible, miracles cannot prove a prophet's truthfulness. This is a logical reduction to an absurd consequence.
The proof relies on the threat of indistinguishable sources of miracles.
4
Reflect on the importance for prophethood
Consider how this argument defends the orthodox view that only Allah performs miracles through prophets. If humans could do it, the link between miracle and truth would break.
This proof is part of a larger debate on human agency and divine action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان التاسع
نقول للمعتزلة: إذا جوزتم كون العبد موجداً. فما الأمان من أن يكون محدث المعجزات واحداً من الشياطين والأبالسة. وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه يخرج المعجز من أن يدل على الصدق؟
The ninth proof: We say to the Mu'tazila: If you permit the servant to be an originator (mujid), then what assurance is there that the one who brings about miracles (al-mu'jizat) might be one of the devils (al-shayatin) and demons (al-abalisah)? On this assumption, the miracle would cease to indicate truthfulness.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a proof (al-burhan al-tasi') that refutes the Mu'tazilite doctrine that humans create their own actions. The author argues by reductio ad absurdum: if a human can be a true originator of actions (mujid), then there is no guarantee that miracles are performed only by prophets. In fact, devils and demons could also produce miracles. Since miracles are supposed to be proof of a prophet's truthfulness, this would invalidate them as evidence. The argument is concise and relies on the impossibility of distinguishing between a prophet and a devil if both can originate actions.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الموجد
المعجز
الشياطين
الأبالسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that this proof denies that miracles happen at all, or that it argues that miracles are impossible.
Correction: The proof does not deny miracles; it argues that if humans could originate acts, miracles could be performed by non-prophets, including devils, thus losing their evidential value. The proof actually defends the orthodox view that miracles are divine signs confirming prophethood.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the ninth proof against the Mu'tazila?
A) Humans cannot perform miracles.
B) If humans can create actions, miracles could be performed by devils, undermining their evidential value.
C) Miracles are impossible.
D) Prophets are devils.

Key Takeaway
The ninth proof shows that accepting human origination of acts undermines the proof-value of miracles for prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you claim to have a spiritual experience or answered prayer, how can you be certain it is from God and not from your own desires or even from a deceptive source? What test from this lesson would you apply?
?
The Mu'tazila trusted human ability to originate good actions. In your own life, do you rely more on your own efforts or on God's guidance to know the truth? What would change if you truly believed miracles prove nothing without divine origin?
?
The devils could supposedly produce wonders. Look at your own achievements and successes: are they built on pride and self-reliance, or are they signs of God's favor? How can you tell the difference, and what will you do to ensure your life testifies to God's truth, not your own?

Torah Prophecy: The Blessing of Abraham's Sons
The author presents the first proof of prophethood from the Torah: the blessing on Abraham's sons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the blessing of Abraham upon Ishmael and Isaac in the Torah is interpreted as a prophecy of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
The blessing on Abraham's sons in Genesis points to Muhammad as the promised prophet.

This lesson explores the first of three proofs the author presents for prophethood: prophecies in the Torah. Specifically, we examine the promise of blessing given to Abraham for his sons Ishmael and Isaac, and how Jewish and Islamic interpretations connect this to kingship and prophethood, ultimately pointing to Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how the author introduces the argument from Torah prophecies as the first of three aspects.
The passage begins by linking denial of human agency to difficulty in accepting prophethood.
2
Identify the three blessings
The Torah mentions blessings on Abraham, Isaac, and Ishmael. Find these in the text and understand that Jewish scholars interpret 'blessing' as kingship and prophethood.
3
Understand the interpretation
Jewish scholars see the blessing on Isaac fulfilled through Moses and the kings of Israel. The author then argues that the blessing on Ishmael points to a future great nation and a prophet—Muhammad.
The author quotes Quranic verses to confirm that both Ishmael and Isaac were blessed.
4
Examine the Torah verses
Read the three quotes from Genesis (22:16-18, 17:15-16, 17:18-20) and see how they describe blessings of nations, kings, and a great nation—all pointing to Ishmael's descendants.
These verses are the core textual evidence for the prophecy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالله التوفيق وأما بيان أن كل من نفى كون العبد موجداً، فإنه يتعذر عليه الاعتراف بالنبوة ) فبيانه من ثلاثة وجوه : (۱) في التوراة ، وفي الإنجيل : نبوءات واضحة الدلالة على نبي الإسلام، محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم . نذكر منها : أولاً : البشارة بنبي الإسلام في التوراة أولاً : جاء في سفر التكوين : أن الله تعالى وعد إبراهيم عليه السلام بأن يطرح البركة في ولديه أ - إسماعيل ب - وإسحق . وقد فسر علماء اليهود البركة بأنها تعني أ - الملك ب - والنبوة أي يكون من نسل إسحق : نبي وملوك على الشعوب. ويقولون إن بركة إسحق عليه السلام قد تحققت . فإنه أنجب يعقوب ، ومن سلالة يعقوب جاء النبي موسى عليه السلام بالتوراة . وقد انتشر اليهود في الأرض الماً ، وحكموا وعلموا . كما قال تعالى : ( وإذ قال موسى لقومه : يا قوم اذكروا نعمة الله عليكم . إذ جعل فيكم أنبياء ، وجعلكم ملوكاً . وآتاكم ما لم يؤت أحداً من العالمين ) [ سورة المائدة ، آية ٢٠ ] والتوراة نصت على ۱ - بركة إبراهيم ٢ - وعلى بركة لإسحق ٢ - وعلى بركة الإسماعيل . كما نص القرآن في قوله تعالى : فإرحمت الله وبركاته عليكم أهل البيت ) [ سورة هود ، آية : ۷۳] وفي قوله تعالى : ( وباركنا عليه ، وعلى إسحق ) [ سورة الصافات ، آية : ۱۱۳] أي على إسماعيل الذبيح ، وإسحق أخيه . وهذا هو نص التوراة في البركة : . ١ - ه بذاتي أقسمت يقول الحرب : إني من أجل أنك فعلت هذا الأمر ، ولم تمسك ابنك وحيدك . أباركك ماركة. ويتبارك في نسلك جميع أمم الأرض . من أجل أنك سمعت لقولي ، [ تكوين ۲۲ : ١٦ - ٢١٨ - : وقال الله لإبراهيم : ساراى امرأتك لا تدعوا اسمها ساراي، بل اسمها سارة ، وأباركها وأعطيك أيضاً منها ابناً. أباركها فتكون اسماً . وملوك شعوب منها يكونون : [ تکوین ۱۷ : ١٥ - ١٦ ] ٣ - « وقال إبراهيم الله : ليت إسماعيل يعيش أمامك ؟ فقال الله : وأما إسماعيل فقد سمعت لك فيه . ها أنا أباركه . وأثمره . وأكثره كثيراً جداً . أثنى عشر رئياً بلد واجعله أمة كبيرة . [ تکوین ۱۷ : ۱۸ - ۲۰ ] .
And by God is success. As for the demonstration that whoever denies that the servant is an agent, then it becomes impossible for him to recognize prophethood—its demonstration is from three aspects: (1) In the Torah and in the Gospel there are prophecies clearly indicative of the Prophet of Islam, Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. We mention from them: First: The good news of the Prophet of Islam in the Torah. First: It came in the Book of Genesis that God Almighty promised Abraham, peace be upon him, to bestow blessing upon his two sons: Ishmael and Isaac. And the Jewish scholars interpreted the blessing as meaning kingship and prophethood: that from the descendants of Isaac would come a prophet and kings over the peoples. And they say that the blessing of Isaac was fulfilled, for he fathered Jacob, and from the lineage of Jacob came the Prophet Moses, peace be upon him, with the Torah. And the Jews spread in the land [as a mother?], ruled, and taught. As God Almighty said: 'And [mention] when Moses said to his people, 'O my people, remember the favor of God upon you when He appointed among you prophets and made you kings and gave you that which He had not given anyone among the worlds.'' [Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:20] And the Torah stipulated: 1) The blessing of Abraham, 2) The blessing for Isaac, 3) And the blessing of Ishmael. As the Quran stipulated in His saying: 'The mercy of God and His blessings be upon you, people of the house' [Surah Hud, 11:73] and in His saying: 'And We blessed him and Isaac' [Surah al-Saffat, 37:113] meaning Ishmael the sacrificed and his brother Isaac. And this is the text of the Torah regarding the blessing: 1. 'By myself I have sworn, says the Lord, because you have done this thing, and have not withheld your son, your only son, I will surely bless you [with blessing?]. And in your seed all the nations of the earth shall be blessed, because you have obeyed my voice.' [Genesis 22:16-18] - And God said to Abraham: 'Sarai your wife, you shall not call her name Sarai, but her name shall be Sarah. I will bless her and also give you a son from her. I will bless her so that she shall be a mother of nations; kings of peoples shall come from her.' [Genesis 17:15-16] 3. 'And Abraham said to God: 'Oh that Ishmael might live before you!' And God said: 'As for Ishmael, I have heard you. I will bless him and make him fruitful and multiply him exceedingly. He shall beget twelve princes, and I will make him a great nation.' [Genesis 17:18-20].
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage introduces a new argument: denial of human agency leads to impossibility of recognizing prophethood. The author then lists three proofs, starting with prophecies in the Torah and Gospel. He focuses first on the Torah: the blessing of Abraham upon Ishmael and Isaac. Jewish scholars interpret 'blessing' as kingship and prophethood. The blessing of Isaac was fulfilled through Moses and the kings of Israel. The author then cites Torah verses and Quranic verses to show that both Ishmael and Isaac were blessed. The actual Torah quotes from Genesis are given.

Key Terms
نبوءات
التوراة
البشارة
إبراهيم
إسماعيل
إسحق
البركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Torah explicitly names Muhammad as a prophet.
Correction: The author does not claim that the Torah explicitly names Muhammad. Rather, he argues that the blessings and promises of kingship and prophethood in Abraham's lineage point to a future prophet, which Muslims identify as Muhammad.

Checkpoint
What is the first proof the author gives for prophethood?
A) A prophecy in the Gospel.
B) The blessing of Abraham on his sons in the Torah.
C) The Quranic verses about Moses.
D) The argument from miracles.

Key Takeaway
The Torah's blessing on Abraham's sons, interpreted as kingship and prophethood, is seen as a prophecy pointing to the coming of Muhammad as a prophet from the line of Ishmael.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Torah's blessing on Ishmael includes 'all nations of the earth shall be blessed through your seed.' If you believe Muhammad is that seed, how does that change the way you view the previous scriptures and their connection to your faith? Are you living as if that blessing is for you?
?
The author uses Jewish interpretation of 'blessing' as 'kingship and prophethood.' If that interpretation is correct, what does it mean for you that the blessing on Ishmael has been fulfilled in the Arab nation and Muhammad? How should that affect your gratitude and commitment to the Prophet's teachings?
?
God made a promise to Abraham that his sons would be blessed. Do you see yourself as part of that ongoing blessing through your belief in Muhammad? If so, what responsibility do you have to uphold that blessing and pass it on to others?

Prophethood

6 min
First Proof from Torah: Blessing on Ishmael and Isaac Prefigures Muhammad
First biblical proof: God's blessing on both Ishmael and Isaac implies a prophet from Ishmael's line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the blessing promised to Abraham's sons Ishmael and Isaac in the Torah is used to prove that Muhammad is the prophesied prophet from Ishmael's line.

Core Idea
The blessing on Isaac was fulfilled in Moses; the blessing on Ishmael must be fulfilled in Muhammad.

In this passage, the author presents a scriptural argument from the Torah to demonstrate that the prophethood of Muhammad was foretold in earlier scriptures. He focuses on the blessing God promised to Abraham for both his sons, Ishmael and Isaac, and explains how Jewish scholars interpret that blessing as kingship and prophethood. By showing that the blessing on Isaac was realized in Moses, he argues that the same blessing on Ishmael must be realized in a prophet who brings a new law—identified as Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Notice the structure: opening claim, Torah citations, interpretation, and conclusion.
The passage contains direct quotes from Genesis; you may recognize them.
2
Identify the two blessings
Find where the author mentions the blessing on Isaac and the blessing on Ishmael. Note how the author interprets 'blessing' as kingship and prophethood based on Jewish interpretation.
The author quotes Genesis 17 and 22.
3
Understand the symmetry argument
The author argues: since the blessing on Isaac was fulfilled in Moses (a prophet with a law), the blessing on Ishmael must also be fulfilled in a prophet with a law. Ask yourself why this symmetry is persuasive.
This is the core reasoning for identifying Muhammad.
4
Analyze the Torah quotes
Read the three Torah passages cited: Genesis 22:16-18 (blessing on Abraham), Genesis 17:15-16 (blessing on Isaac), Genesis 17:18-20 (blessing on Ishmael). Notice how each supports the claim.
The author uses these to show the blessing applies to both sons.
5
Connect to the Quranic verse
The author ends by quoting Surah al-Muzzammil 73:15, which likens Muhammad's mission to Moses'. Reflect on how this Quranic verse strengthens the argument.
This ties the Torah proof to Islamic revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان أن كل من نفى كون العبد موجداً ، فإنه يتعذر عليه الاعتراف بالنبوة ) فبيانه من ثلاثة وجوه : (۱) في التوراة ، وفي الإنجيل : نبوءات واضحة الدلالة على نبي الإسلام ، محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم . نذكر منها : أولاً : البشارة بنبي الإسلام في التوراة أولاً : جاء في سفر التكوين : أن الله تعالى وعد إبراهيم عليه السلام بأن يطرح البركة في ولديه أ - إسماعيل ب - وإسحق . وقد فسر علماء اليهود البركة بأنها تعني أ - الملك ب - والنبوة أي يكون من نسل إسحق : نبي وملوك على الشعوب. ويقولون إن بركة إسحق عليه السلام قد تحققت . فإنه أنجب يعقوب ، ومن سلالة يعقوب جاء النبي موسى عليه السلام بالتوراة . وقد انتشر اليهود في الأرض الماً [؟] ، وحكموا وعلموا . كما قال تعالى : ( وإذ قال موسى لقومه : يا قوم اذكروا نعمة الله عليكم . إذ جعل فيكم أنبياء ، وجعلكم ملوكاً . وآتاكم ما لم يؤت أحداً من العالمين ) [ سورة المائدة ، آية ٢٠ ] والتوراة نصت على ۱ - بركة إبراهيم ٢ - وعلى بركة لإسحق ٢ - وعلى بركة الإسماعيل . كما نص القرآن في قوله تعالى : فإرحمت الله وبركاته عليكم أهل البيت ) [ سورة هود ، آية : ۷۳] وفي قوله تعالى : ( وباركنا عليه ، وعلى إسحق ) [ سورة الصافات ، آية : ۱۱۳] أي على إسماعيل الذبيح ، وإسحق أخيه . وهذا هو نص التوراة في البركة : . ١ - ه بذاتي أقسمت يقول الحرب [؟] : إني من أجل أنك فعلت هذا الأمر ، ولم تمسك ابنك وحيدك . أباركك ماركة [؟] . ويتبارك في نسلك جميع أمم الأرض . من أجل أنك سمعت لقولي ، [ تكوين ٢٢ : ١٦ - ٢١٨ [؟] - : وقال الله لإبراهيم : ساراى امرأتك لا تدعوا اسمها ساراي، بل اسمها سارة ، وأباركها وأعطيك أيضاً منها ابناً. أباركها فتكون اسماً . وملوك شعوب منها يكونون : [ تكوین ۱۷ : ١٥ - ١٦ ] ٣ - « وقال إبراهيم الله : ليت إسماعيل يعيش أمامك ؟ فقال الله : وأما إسماعيل فقد سمعت لك فيه . ها أنا أباركه . وأثمره . وأكثره كثيراً جداً . أثنى عشر رئياً بلد [؟] واجعله أمة كبيرة . [ تكوین ۱۷ : ١٨ - ۲۰ ] . من هذه النصوص يتبين لنا : أن البركة الموعود بها إبراهيم وهي على تفسير اليهود . تعني والنبوة . هي الإسماعيل كما هي الإسحق. وحيث تحققت مع بني إسحق في شخص نبي ، بدات البركة من ظهوره لأنه صاحب شريعة. لا بد وأن تتحقق مع بني إسماعيل في شخص نبي ، تبدأ بركة إسماعيل من ظهوره . والتاريخ يشهد : ان صاحب الشريعة في نسل إسحق هو موسى . ويشهد أن صاحب الشريعة في نسل إسماعيل هو محمد . ولذلك جاء في القرآن الكريم أن محمداً مماثل لموسى في قوله تعالى : ( إنا أرسلنا إليكم رسولاً شاهداً عليكم ، كما أرسلنا إلى فرعون رسولاً ) [ المزمل ١٥ ] .
And as for the demonstration that whoever denies that the servant is the creator [of his actions] finds it impossible to acknowledge prophethood: its demonstration is from three aspects. (1) In the Torah and the Gospel there are prophecies clearly indicating the Prophet of Islam, Muhammad, peace be upon him. We mention from them: First: the glad tidings of the Prophet of Islam in the Torah. First: It came in the Book of Genesis that God Almighty promised Abraham, peace be upon him, to place the blessing in his two sons: A) Ishmael, B) Isaac. And the Jewish scholars interpreted the blessing as meaning: A) kingship, B) prophethood, i.e., from the descendants of Isaac will be a prophet and kings over the peoples. And they say that the blessing of Isaac, peace be upon him, has been fulfilled. For he begot Jacob, and from the lineage of Jacob came the prophet Moses, peace be upon him, with the Torah. And the Jews spread in the earth [?], and ruled and taught. As the Exalted said: 'And when Moses said to his people: O my people, remember the favor of Allah upon you when He appointed among you prophets and made you kings and gave you what He had not given anyone among the worlds' [Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 20]. And the Torah stipulated: 1) the blessing of Abraham, 2) and the blessing for Isaac, 3) and the blessing for Ishmael. As the Qur'an stated in the saying of the Exalted: 'The mercy of Allah and His blessings be upon you, O people of the house' [Surah Hud, verse 73], and in His saying: 'And We blessed him and Isaac' [Surah al-Saffat, verse 113], meaning Ishmael the sacrifice and Isaac his brother. And this is the text of the Torah concerning the blessing: 1. 'I swear by Myself, says the Lord [?], that because you have done this thing and have not withheld your only son, I will bless you and [?] and in your descendants all the nations of the earth shall be blessed, because you have obeyed My voice' [Genesis 22:16-18]. And God said to Abraham: 'Sarai your wife, you shall not call her name Sarai, but her name shall be Sarah. And I will bless her and also give you a son from her. I will bless her, and she shall be a mother of nations; kings of peoples shall come from her' [Genesis 17:15-16]. 3. 'And Abraham said to God: O that Ishmael might live before You! God said: But as for Ishmael, I have heard you. Behold, I will bless him and make him fruitful and multiply him greatly. He shall become twelve princes [?] and I will make him a great nation' [Genesis 17:18-20]. From these texts it becomes clear to us that the blessing promised to Abraham—and according to the interpretation of the Jews it means kingship and prophethood—is for Ishmael as it is for Isaac. And since it was fulfilled with the descendants of Isaac in the person of a prophet, the blessing began from his appearance because he was the possessor of a law. It must be fulfilled with the descendants of Ishmael in the person of a prophet, the blessing of Ishmael begins from his appearance. And history bears witness that the possessor of the law in the lineage of Isaac is Moses. And it bears witness that the possessor of the law in the lineage of Ishmael is Muhammad. Therefore it came in the Noble Qur'an that Muhammad is similar to Moses in His saying: 'Indeed, We have sent to you a messenger as a witness upon you, just as We sent to Pharaoh a messenger' [Surah al-Muzzammil, verse 15].
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the overall argument: anyone who denies that the servant is the creator of his actions cannot consistently acknowledge prophethood. The proof is given in three ways, and here the first way is detailed: prophecies in the Torah and Gospel clearly point to Muhammad. The author focuses on the Torah, starting with the blessing on Abraham's two sons, Ishmael and Isaac. Jewish scholars interpret 'blessing' as kingship and prophethood. The blessing on Isaac was fulfilled in Moses, who brought the Torah. Similarly, the blessing on Ishmael must be fulfilled in a prophet who brings a law (shari'a). History shows that the law-bringer from Isaac's line is Moses, and from Ishmael's line is Muhammad. The author then cites Quranic verses to support that Muhammad is similar to Moses. The passage includes the actual Torah texts from Genesis about the blessings, which the author then interprets to conclude that Muhammad is the promised prophet from Ishmael's line.

Key Terms
بركة (blessing)
نبوة (prophethood)
شريعة (law)
بشارة (glad tidings)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is citing the Torah as authoritative scripture for Muslims.
Correction: The author uses the Torah as a source of prophecy that foretold Muhammad, consistent with the Islamic belief that previous scriptures contain predictions of the final prophet. He is not endorsing the Torah as uncorrupted, but as still containing traces of the original revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what does the blessing on Isaac that was fulfilled in Moses prove about the blessing on Ishmael?
A) It was not a true blessing
B) It must also be fulfilled in a prophet with a law
C) It was fulfilled in the Jewish kings
D) It was only for Isaac's lineage

Key Takeaway
The blessing on Isaac was fulfilled in Moses; therefore, the blessing on Ishmael must be fulfilled in a prophet with a law—identified as Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson proves that God's blessing on Ishmael was fulfilled through Muhammad. You are from that blessed nation. When you look at your life, are you living as a recipient of that blessing? What specific action will you take today to honor that prophethood in your daily choices?
?
The author uses a logical argument from scripture to affirm Muhammad's prophethood. Is your own conviction based on such evidence, or is it just inherited? Ask yourself: if you had to defend this proof tomorrow, would you be able to? What step can you take this week to deepen your certainty?
?
God's promise to Abraham included both kingship and prophethood. The kingship of the Muslim ummah has been lost in many lands. Do you feel a personal loss for that? What are you doing to restore the honor of this ummah in your own sphere of influence?

Second Proof from Deuteronomy: The Prophet Like Moses
Second biblical proof from Deuteronomy 18: a prophet like Moses, from Ishmael's line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second biblical proof from Deuteronomy 18, which predicts a prophet like Moses who must come from Ishmael's lineage, and how the nine attributes fit Muhammad.

Core Idea
Deuteronomy 18 predicts a prophet like Moses—and only Muhammad qualifies.

This lesson examines a second biblical proof from the Torah: the promise in Deuteronomy 18 of a prophet 'like Moses.' The author argues that this prophet cannot be from the Israelites because the Torah itself says no such prophet will arise from them. Instead, he must come from the line of Ishmael, and the nine attributes listed in the text all point to Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the Deuteronomy passage
Begin by reading the Arabic quotation from Deuteronomy 18:15-22. Notice the key phrases: 'a prophet like me,' 'from your brothers,' and 'I will put My words in his mouth.'
2
Understand the argument about Ishmael
The author deduces that the promised prophet must be from Ishmael's descendants. He uses two reasons: the blessing on Ishmael in Genesis, and the Torah's statement that no prophet like Moses will come from Israel.
The phrase 'from your brothers' is interpreted as from a related people, not Israel itself.
3
Examine the nine attributes
The author lists nine attributes from the text that describe the awaited prophet: prophet, from Ishmael, like Moses in miracles, illiterate, abrogator of the law, trustworthy, judge over Israel, non-killing, and speaker of the unseen. See how each is grounded in the Deuteronomy quote.
4
Connect to Muhammad
The author concludes that all nine attributes apply to Muhammad. Reflect on how each attribute is fulfilled in his life and mission.
This proof is part of a larger series of biblical arguments for Muhammad's prophethood.

Source Text

ثانياً : جاء في الاصحاح الثامن عشر من سفر التثنية هذا النص : و يقيم لك الرب إلهك : نبياً من وسطك . من إخوتك . مثلي . له تسمعون أقيم لهم : نبياً من وسط إخوتهم . مثلك وأجعل كلامي في فمه . فيكلمهم بكل ما أوصيه به . ويكون أن الإنسان الذي لا يسمع لكلامي الذي يتكلم به باسمي . أنا أطالبه وأما النبي الذي يطغى فيتكلم باسمي كلاماً لم أوصه أن يتكلم به أو الذي يتكلم باسم آلهة أخرى. فيموت ذلك النبي . وإن قلت في قلبك : كيف تعرف الكلام الذي لم يتكلم به الرب ؟ فما تكلم به النبي باسم الرب ، ولم يحدث ولم يصر ، فهو الكلام الذي لم يتكلم به الرب . بل يطغيان تكلم به النبي ، فلا تخف منه : [ التثنية ١٨ : ١٥ - ٢٢ ] . ومن هذا النص يتبين مجيء نبي بعد موسى عليه السلام. وهذا النبي لا بد وأن يكون من نسل إسماعيل . لأن الإسماعيل بركة. وهذا النص يوضح أوصاف النبي الأتي بتسعة أوصاف : 1 - نبي ٢ - من بني إسماعيل لقوله من وسط إخوتهم ولقوله في سفر التكوين إن لإسماعيل بركة ٣ - مثل موسى في المعجزات والانتصار على الأعداء في الحروب. وقد نصت التوراة في آخر سـفــر التثنية بأنه لن يأتي نبي في المستقبل من بني إسرائيل مثل موسى . وحيث أن الإسماعيل بركة ، ولن يأتي مماثل لموسى من اليهود ، ونص النبوءة بقول عن النبي المنتظر : إنه مثل موسى . يكون النبي المنتظر هو محمد . ٤ - أمي . لا يقرأ ولا يكتب : واجعل كلامي في فمه ، فمه ، ٥ - ينسخ شريعة موسى و له تسمعون : : 1 - أمين على الوحي الإلهي ( فيكلمهم بكل ما أوصيه به ، ۷ - يقضي على ملك بني إسرائيل في العالم ، ويكون أن الإنسان الذي لا يسمع لكلامي الذي يتكلم : أنا أطالبه : به باسمي : ، وفي بعض التراجم : أنا أنتة منه وأهلكه ٨- لا يقتل : « وأما النبي الذي يطغى الخ ، ٩ - يتحدث عن غيب ويقع في مستقبل الأيام ، وإن قلت في قلبك ... الخ ، والأوصاف كلها تنطبق على محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
Secondly: It came in the eighteenth chapter of the Book of Deuteronomy this text: 'The Lord your God will raise up for you a prophet from your midst, from your brothers, like me. To him you shall listen. I will raise up for them a prophet from among their brothers, like you, and I will put My words in his mouth, and he shall speak to them all that I command him. And it shall be that whoever will not listen to My words which he speaks in My name, I will require it of him. But the prophet who presumes to speak a word in My name which I have not commanded him to speak, or who speaks in the name of other gods, that prophet shall die. And if you say in your heart, “How shall we know the word which the Lord has not spoken?” When a prophet speaks in the name of the Lord, and the thing does not happen or come to pass, that is the word which the Lord has not spoken; the prophet has spoken it presumptuously; you shall not be afraid of him.' [Deuteronomy 18:15-22]. And from this text, the coming of a prophet after Moses, peace be upon him, is evident. And this prophet must be from the descendants of Ishmael, because Ishmael has a blessing. And this text clarifies the attributes of the coming prophet in nine attributes: 1) Prophet, 2) From the sons of Ishmael, because of his saying 'from their brothers' and his saying in Genesis that Ishmael has a blessing, 3) Like Moses in miracles and victory over enemies in battles. And the Torah stated at the end of Deuteronomy that no prophet will come in the future from the Children of Israel like Moses. And since Ishmael has a blessing, and no one like Moses will come from the Jews, and the text of the prophecy says about the awaited prophet: he is like Moses, then the awaited prophet is Muhammad. 4) Illiterate, not reading or writing: 'and I will put My words in his mouth', 5) He abrogates the law of Moses, and 'to him you shall listen', 6) Trustworthy over divine revelation: 'he shall speak to them all that I command him', 7) He judges over the kingdom of the Children of Israel in the world, and 'whoever will not listen to My words which he speaks in My name, I will require it of him', and in some translations: 'I will take vengeance and destroy him', 8) He does not kill: 'But the prophet who presumes ...', 9) He speaks about the unseen and it occurs in future days, 'and if you say in your heart ...' etc. And all the attributes apply to Muhammad, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents the second biblical proof from Deuteronomy 18. The author first quotes the passage in Arabic, then explains that it predicts a prophet after Moses. This prophet must be from the descendants of Ishmael because the earlier blessing on Ishmael implies a prophet from his line. The author then lists nine attributes from the text that apply to Muhammad. Notably, the Torah itself says no prophet like Moses will arise from Israel again, so the promised prophet like Moses must be from Ishmael's line—i.e., Muhammad. The attributes include being illiterate (ummi), abrogating previous law, faithfulness to revelation, judgment over Israel, etc. The author concludes that all these fit Muhammad.

Key Terms
نبي مثل موسى (prophet like Moses)
أمي (illiterate)
نسخ (abrogation)
إخوة (brothers)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think 'from your brothers' refers to fellow Israelites, implying the prophet will come from Israel.
Correction: The author argues that since no prophet like Moses will arise from Israel (as stated in the Torah), 'brothers' must refer to a related people, specifically the Ishmaelites, who are descendants of Abraham through Ishmael.

Checkpoint
Why does the author claim the prophet predicted in Deuteronomy must be from Ishmael and not from Isaac?
A) Because the Torah says no prophet like Moses will come from Israel
B) Because Ishmael was the firstborn
C) Because the blessing on Isaac was already fulfilled
D) Because the text says 'from your midst'

Key Takeaway
Deuteronomy 18 contains a prophecy of a prophet like Moses, and Muhammad perfectly fulfills the nine attributes listed in that prophecy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Muhammad is the prophet like Moses, with all the signs fulfilled? Or do you hold back in your heart? What would it take for you to submit completely?
?
If the nine attributes from Deuteronomy perfectly describe Muhammad, then his message is from God. Are you living as if you have heard God's words from his mouth? Where are you disobeying?
?
The source says the prophet speaks about the unseen and it occurs. Muhammad's prophecies about the future have come true. Does that not demand a response of trust and obedience from you today? What are you waiting for?

The Scepter Shall Not Depart: A Biblical Prophecy
Third biblical proof: Jacob's prophecy about Shiloh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Genesis 49:10 is interpreted as a prophecy of the Prophet Muhammad based on the departure of kingship from Israel.

Core Idea
The scepter leaving Judah points to a non-Israelite prophet – Muhammad.

This lesson examines a third biblical proof from Jacob's prophecy to Judah. The author argues that the coming of 'Shiloh' marks the end of Jewish kingship and law, implying Shiloh must be from outside Israel. This leads to identifying Shiloh as the Prophet of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the biblical citation and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Note the quote from Genesis 49:10 and the author's interpretation.
The word 'Shiloh' is key – it means 'the Prophet of Safety' according to the author.
2
Understand the interpretation of symbols
The author explains 'scepter' as kingship and 'lawgiver' as the Torah law. Recognize that this sets up the condition for Shiloh's coming.
3
Grasp the key inference
Why must Shiloh be from outside Israel? Because the text says kingship will depart when Shiloh appears. If Shiloh were from Israel, kingship would continue.
This is the central logical move in the proof.
4
Connect to Muhammad as the blessed prophet
The author identifies Shiloh as Muhammad, citing the blessing on Ishmael's lineage. Consider how this fits the broader argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً : في الأصحاح التاسع والأربعين من سفر التكوين قول يعقوب لبنيه : و لا يزول قضيب من يهوذا ومشترع من بين رجليه ، حتى يأتي شيلون. وله يكون خضوع شعوب ، [ تكوين ٤٩ : ١٠] أي لا يزول الملك من بني إسرائيل ، ولا تنسخ شريعتهم ، شريعة التوراة ، حتى يأتي نبي الأمان . ولا بد وأن يكون شيلون من غير بني إسرائيل . لأن النص يوضح زوال الملك منهم إذا ظهر شيلون. ولو كان هو منهم لاستمر الملك ولم يزل. والمراد منه : نبي الاسلام لثبوت بركة في نسل إسماعيل عليه السلام
Thirdly: In the forty-ninth chapter of the Book of Genesis, the saying of Jacob to his sons: 'The scepter shall not depart from Judah, nor a lawgiver from between his feet, until Shiloh comes; and to him shall be the obedience of the peoples.' [Genesis 49:10] That is, the kingship shall not depart from the Children of Israel, nor shall their law, the law of the Torah, be abrogated until the Prophet of Safety comes. And Shiloh must be from other than the Children of Israel, because the text clarifies that kingship will depart from them when Shiloh appears. And if he were from them, the kingship would continue and not depart. And what is meant by it is the Prophet of Islam, due to the established blessing in the lineage of Ishmael, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents the third biblical proof from Genesis 49:10. The author interprets Jacob's prophecy: the scepter (kingship) and lawgiver (law) will not depart from Judah until Shiloh comes. The author argues that since Shiloh's arrival causes the departure of kingship and law from Israel, Shiloh cannot be from Israel himself; otherwise the kingship would continue. Therefore, Shiloh must be from outside Israel. The author identifies Shiloh as the Prophet of Islam, Muhammad, because the blessing on Ishmael guarantees a prophet from his line.

Key Terms
شيلون (Shiloh)
قضيب (scepter)
مشترع (lawgiver)
الملك (kingship)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'Shiloh' refers to a place or a Jewish messiah.
Correction: The author argues that Shiloh must be a non-Jewish prophet because the prophecy states kingship will depart when Shiloh appears, which would not happen if Shiloh were from Israel.

Checkpoint
Why does the author conclude that Shiloh cannot be from the Children of Israel?
A) Because Shiloh means 'peace'
B) Because the text says kingship will depart when Shiloh appears
C) Because Jacob was not an Israelite
D) Because the scepter belongs to Judah

Key Takeaway
Jacob's prophecy shows that the coming prophet would be from outside Israel, fulfilling the blessing on Ishmael.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This prophecy was hidden in the Torah for centuries before it was fulfilled. Do you truly believe that Allah prepared the entire history of the world for the coming of Muhammad ﷺ? If you are certain, then why do you still hesitate to make his teachings the absolute guide for your daily decisions? What one step will you take today to honor this divine plan?
?
The scepter had to depart from Israel for the final prophet to come. Has your attachment to any worldly power, status, or lineage kept you from submitting fully to the truth? What 'scepter' in your life – a position, a relationship, a habit – do you need to release so that the Messenger can truly rule your heart?
?
If the blessing on Ishmael's line was so significant that it produced the greatest prophet, then who are the 'blessed ones' in your life that you have overlooked? Today, will you recognize and honor someone whom Allah has chosen to be a source of blessing for you, even if they are not from your own 'lineage'?

The Blessing of Abraham and the Lawgiver from Ishmael
The author presents an argument from the Abrahamic blessing to identify Muhammad as the lawgiver from Ishmael.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the blessing promised to Abraham is used to argue that Muhammad is the lawgiver from Ishmael's lineage, similar to Moses.

Core Idea
The blessing of Abraham requires a lawgiver from Ishmael, fulfilled in Muhammad.

This passage presents a key argument from the Abrahamic blessing: the promise of prophethood was for both Isaac and Ishmael. Since it was realized in Isaac's line through Moses, it must also be realized in Ishmael's line through a lawgiver. The author identifies Muhammad as that lawgiver, citing the Quran to show his similarity to Moses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the logical structure: a premise about the blessing, two parallel cases, and a conclusion supported by history and Quran.
The first word 'الملك' may be a fragment from the previous page; focus on the argument.
2
Identify the main claim
The author claims that the blessing (prophethood) is for Ishmael as it is for Isaac. Trace how this leads to the conclusion that Muhammad is the lawgiver from Ishmael.
Pay attention to the phrase 'صاحب شريعة' (possessor of a law).
3
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
The author quotes Quran 73:15 to show that Muhammad is similar to Moses. Consider how this verse supports the argument that Muhammad is the predicted lawgiver.
The verse is about sending a messenger as a witness, similar to sending Moses to Pharaoh.

الملك من هذه النصوص يتبين لنا : أن البركة الموعود بها إبراهيم وهي على تفسير اليهود . تعني والنبوة . هي الإسماعيل كما هي الإسحق. وحيث تحققت مع بني إسحق في شخص نبي ، بدات البركة من ظهوره لأنه صاحب شريعة. لا بد وأن تتحقق مع بني إسماعيل في شخص نبي ، تبدأ بركة إسماعيل من ظهوره . والتاريخ يشهد : ان صاحب الشريعة في نسل إسحق هو موسى . ويشهد أن صاحب الشريعة في نسل إسماعيل هو محمد . ولذلك جاء في القرآن الكريم أن محمداً مماثل لموسى في قوله تعالى : ( إنا أرسلنا إليكم رسولاً شاهداً عليكم ، كما أرسلنا إلى فرعون رسولاً ) [ المزمل ١٥ ] .
The kingdom: From these texts it becomes clear to us: that the blessing promised to Abraham, and according to the interpretation of the Jews, means prophethood, is for Ishmael as it is for Isaac. When it was realized with the children of Isaac in a person of a prophet, the blessing began from his appearance because he is a possessor of a law. It must be realized with the children of Ishmael in a person of a prophet; the blessing of Ishmael begins from his appearance. And history testifies that the possessor of the law in the lineage of Isaac is Moses, and it testifies that the possessor of the law in the lineage of Ishmael is Muhammad. Therefore it came in the Noble Quran that Muhammad is similar to Moses in His saying the Exalted: 'Indeed, We have sent to you a Messenger as a witness upon you, just as We sent to Pharaoh a Messenger' [Al-Muzzammil 15].
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents an argument from the blessing of Abraham. The author, likely Al-Asfahani or similar, states that the blessing promised to Abraham, according to Jewish interpretation, includes prophethood and is equally for Ishmael as for Isaac. After the blessing was realized with Isaac's descendants through Moses, it must also be realized with Ishmael's descendants through a prophet who is a lawgiver, because the blessing began with Moses' appearance. History shows that the lawgiver from Isaac is Moses, and from Ishmael is Muhammad. The author then quotes Quran 73:15 to assert that Muhammad is similar to Moses.

Proof from Deuteronomy 18: The Prophet Like Moses from Among the Brethren
The author quotes Deuteronomy 18:15-22 and lists nine characteristics, concluding they apply to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Deuteronomy 18:15-22 to argue that the awaited prophet must be like Moses, from the brethren of the Israelites (i.e., Ishmaelites), and that all nine characteristics point to Muhammad.

Core Idea
The Deuteronomy prophecy predicts a prophet like Moses from Ishmael, and Muhammad perfectly matches all nine attributes.

The author presents a second proof from the Torah, quoting Deuteronomy 18:15-22. This passage foretells a prophet like Moses who will arise from among the brethren of the Israelites. The author then identifies nine specific characteristics of this prophet and argues that they are all fulfilled in Muhammad, peace be upon him.

Guided Path
1
Read the biblical quote
Read the Arabic quote from Deuteronomy 18:15-22 carefully. Note the description of a prophet like Moses who will speak God's words.
The quote includes the promise of a prophet from 'your brethren'.
2
Understand the interpretation
The author interprets 'your brethren' as referring to the Ishmaelites (Arabs), supporting this with the blessing of Ishmael in Genesis.
This is key to showing the prophet is not from among the Israelites themselves.
3
Review the nine attributes
The author lists nine attributes of the awaited prophet. Go through each one and see how they match Muhammad's life and mission.
Attributes include being illiterate, like Moses in miracles, abrogating Mosaic law, etc.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that all attributes apply to Muhammad. Consider how each attribute is uniquely fulfilled in him.
This is a standard argument in comparative religion.

And since Ishmael is a blessing, and no one similar to Moses will come from the Jews, and the prophecy says about the awaited prophet: he is like Moses, then the awaited prophet is Muhammad. 4 - illiterate, he does not read nor write: and I will put My words in his mouth, his mouth, 5 - he abrogates the law of Moses and to him you shall listen, 6 - trustworthy in divine revelation: he will speak to them all that I command him, 7 - he will destroy the kingdom of the children of Israel in the world: and it shall be that whoever will not hear My words which he speaks in My name, I will require of him; in some translations: I will destroy him, 8 - he will not be killed: but the prophet who presumes... etc., 9 - he speaks about the unseen and it occurs in the future: and if you say in your heart... etc., and all the attributes apply to Muhammad, peace be upon him.

Commentary

He then lists nine characteristics that this prophet must have: 1) a prophet, 2) from the children of Ishmael because 'your brethren' refers to Ishmaelites, 3) like Moses in miracles and victory, 4) illiterate, 5) abrogates the law of Moses, 6) trustworthy in revelation, 7) destroys the kingdom of Israel, 8) not to be killed, 9) speaks of the future and it comes true. He then states that all these characteristics apply to Muhammad.

The Prophecy of Shiloh: A Biblical Proof for Muhammad
Quoting Jacob's prophecy to prove Muhammad as Shiloh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophecy of Shiloh in Genesis 49:10 is interpreted as a proof for the prophethood of Muhammad.

Core Idea
The scepter's departure from Judah points to a prophet from outside Israel.

In this passage, the author presents a third biblical proof for Muhammad's prophethood. He quotes a prophecy from Genesis where Jacob says the scepter will not depart from Judah until Shiloh comes. The author argues that Shiloh cannot be from Judah because the scepter departs when he comes. Therefore, Shiloh must be from another lineage, specifically from Ishmael, and he identifies Shiloh as the Prophet Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text of Genesis 49:10 and its interpretation. Note the key terms: scepter, lawgiver, Shiloh.
The author adds 'prophet of peace' as an interpretation.
2
Understand the logical structure
The author uses a conditional: the scepter remains until Shiloh comes. Therefore, when Shiloh comes, the scepter departs. This implies Shiloh is not from Judah.
3
Identify the target of the prophecy
The author concludes Shiloh is Muhammad, based on biblical blessings on Ishmael's line.
This is a common interfaith argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثاً : في الأصحاح التاسع والأربعين من سفر التكوين قول يعقوب لبنيه : و لا يزول قضيب من يهوذا ومشترع من بين رجليه ، حتى يأتي شيلون. وله يكون خضوع شعوب ، [ تكوين ٤٩ : ١٠] أي لا يزول الملك من بني إسرائيل ، ولا تنسخ شريعتهم ، شريعة التوراة ، حتى يأتي نبي الأمان . ولا بد وأن يكون شيلون من غير بني إسرائيل . لأن النص يوضح زوال الملك منهم إذا ظهر شيلون. ولو كان هو منهم لاستمر الملك ولم يزل. والمراد منه : نبي الاسلام لثبوت بركة في نسل إسماعيل عليه السلام
Thirdly: In the forty-ninth chapter of the book of Genesis, the saying of Jacob to his sons: 'And the scepter shall not depart from Judah, nor a lawgiver from between his feet, until Shiloh comes; and to him shall be the obedience of peoples' [Genesis 49:10]. That is, the kingdom will not depart from the children of Israel, nor will their law, the law of the Torah, be abrogated, until the prophet of peace comes. And it is necessary that Shiloh be from other than the children of Israel, because the text clarifies the removal of the kingdom from them when Shiloh appears. If he were from them, the kingdom would continue and not cease. And the intended meaning is the prophet of Islam, due to the confirmation of the blessing in the descendants of Ishmael, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents a third proof from Genesis 49:10. The author quotes Jacob's prophecy that the scepter will not depart from Judah until Shiloh comes. He interprets 'scepter' as kingship and 'Shiloh' as the prophet of peace. Since the prophecy says the scepter will depart when Shiloh comes, Shiloh cannot be from Judah, because if he were from Judah, the scepter would remain. Therefore Shiloh is from outside the children of Israel, i.e., from Ishmael. The author concludes that Shiloh is the prophet of Islam, Muhammad, because of the blessing established in the descendants of Ishmael.

مشترع
خضوع شعوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Shiloh refers to a place or a Davidic king from Judah.
Correction: The author argues that if Shiloh were from Judah, the scepter would not depart, contradicting the prophecy. Thus Shiloh must be from outside Israel, and he identifies him as Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
The prophecy of Shiloh in Genesis is interpreted as referring to Muhammad, based on the condition that the scepter departs when he comes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The author uses a logical deduction to identify Shiloh as Muhammad. Proof from Deuteronomy 33: Sinai, Seir, and Paran
The author interprets the three locations in Moses' blessing as referring to the three revelations, the last being Quran from Paran/Mecca.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author interprets Deuteronomy 33:1-3 as a prophecy of three revelations, with the final one being the Quran from Paran/Mecca, and the biblical evidence for identifying Paran with Mecca.

Core Idea
The Torah itself points to three revelations, the last from Paran — the Quran.

This lesson examines a proof from the Torah (Deuteronomy 33) where Moses' blessing mentions three locations: Sinai, Seir, and Paran. The author interprets these as referring to the revelations of the Torah, the Jewish interpretive tradition, and finally the Quran revealed to Prophet Muhammad. We will also explore the biblical evidence that Paran is the mountains of Mecca, home of Ishmael's descendants.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to understand the flow of the argument.
The passage cites Deuteronomy 33:1-3 and then provides interpretation.
2
Identify the three locations
Note the three locations: Sinai, Seir, and Paran. The author assigns a specific meaning to each: Sinai for the Torah revelation, Seir for Jewish scholarly activity, and Paran for a clear law (the Quran).
3
Examine evidence for Paran as Mecca
Find the evidence from Genesis that Hagar and Ishmael settled in Paran, and that the author identifies Paran with the mountains of Mecca.
The author also mentions a Greek translation that adds a detail about companions.
4
Understand the conclusion of abrogation
Note the final point: that after the appearance of Prophet Muhammad, the previous law (Torah) is abrogated, and deeds based on it are not accepted.
This is based on the interpretation that the 'myriads of holy ones' refers to the companions coming to Palestine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعا : قال في نهاية التوراة : وهذه هي البركة التي بارك بها موسى رجل الله بني إسرائيل قبل موته . فقال : جاء الرب من سيناء. وأشرق لهم من سعير . وتلالاً من جبال فاران . وأتى من ربوات القدس ، وعن يمينه نار شريعة لهم . فأحب الشعب جميع قديسيه في يدك . وهم جالسون عند قدمك ، يتقبلون من أقوالك . [ تثنية ۳۳ : ١ - ٣] وفي هذا النص نجد الكاتب يخبر عن تقسيم البركة الموعود بها إبراهيم عليه السلام حسب ما جاء عن موسى عليه السلام فقال : إن الله جاء من سيناء ، أي ظهرت شريعته على يد موسى في طور سيناء . ويعني بالإشراق من ساعه : أن علماء بني إسرائيل كانوا يفسرون التوراة في ارض فلسطين والأردن . ويعني بالتلألؤ من جبال فاران: ظهور شريعة واضحة من فاران . والدليل على أن فاران جبال مكة ، وعلى أن فاران موطن بني إسماعيل ما جاء في التوراة أن ملاك الله قابل هاجر وقال لها : « قومي احملي الغلام وشدي ينك به . لأني سأجعله أمة عظيمة ... وكان الله مع الغلام فكبر ، وسكن في البرية ، وكان ينمو رامي قوس . وسكن في برية فاران . [ تكوين ٢٩ ] وفي بعض التراجم - وهي اليونانية - وأق مع ربوات جيش المقدمين ... الخ أي أن اصحاب النبي محمد سيأتون إلى فلسطين لإنهاء الشريعة اليهودية منها إلى غير رجعة . ومن يعمل بها بعد ظهوره لا يقبل عمله لدى الله . لأن الله نسخها على يد محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
Fourthly: He said at the end of the Torah: And this is the blessing with which Moses, the man of God, blessed the children of Israel before his death. He said: 'The LORD came from Sinai, and dawned from Seir upon them; He shone forth from Mount Paran, and He came from the myriads of holy ones; at His right hand was a fiery law for them. Yes, He loves the people; all His saints are in Your hand; they sit down at Your feet; everyone receives Your words' [Deuteronomy 33:1-3]. And in this text we find the writer informing about the division of the promised blessing to Abraham, peace be upon him, according to what came from Moses, peace be upon him. He said: 'The LORD came from Sinai' i.e., His law appeared at the hands of Moses on Mount Sinai. And by 'the dawning from Seir' he means that the scholars of the children of Israel were interpreting the Torah in the land of Palestine and Jordan. And by 'the shining from the mountains of Paran' is the appearance of a clear law from Paran. And the evidence that Paran is the mountains of Mecca, and that Paran is the homeland of the children of Ishmael, is what came in the Torah that the angel of God met Hagar and said to her: 'Arise, take the boy and hold him with your hand, for I will make him a great nation... And God was with the boy, and he grew, and dwelt in the wilderness, and became an archer. And he dwelt in the wilderness of Paran' [Genesis 21:17-21? actually 21:17-21]. And in some translations - the Greek - it says: 'And he came with the myriads of the holy army...' etc., meaning that the companions of the Prophet Muhammad will come to Palestine to end the Jewish law from it irrevocably. And whoever acts by it after his appearance, his deed will not be accepted by God, because God abrogated it at the hands of Muhammad, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents a fourth proof from the end of the Torah, Deuteronomy 33:1-3. The author quotes Moses' blessing where he mentions God coming from Sinai, shining from Seir, and appearing from the mountains of Paran. He interprets these three locations as representing three revelations: Sinai for the revelation of the Torah to Moses, Seir for the interpretation by Jewish scholars in Palestine, and Paran for the revelation of a clear law. He then provides evidence that Paran is the mountains of Mecca, based on the Torah narrative where Hagar and Ishmael settled in the wilderness of Paran. He also cites a Greek translation that adds a mention of the companions of the Prophet Muhammad coming to Palestine to end the Jewish law. He concludes that whoever follows the Jewish law after the appearance of Muhammad will not have his deeds accepted, because God abrogated it through Muhammad.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Paran is a different location, not Mecca.
Correction: The author provides evidence from the Torah (Genesis) that Paran is the wilderness where Ishmael settled, and identifies it with the mountains of Mecca.

Key Takeaway
The author argues that Deuteronomy 33 implicitly prophesies the three major revelations, with the final one from Paran being the Quran, and provides scriptural evidence linking Paran to Mecca.

Glad Tidings of Islam in the Gospel
Introduction to Gospel prophecies and selection of John.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the basis for Islamic claims of prophecies in the Christian Gospels and why the author focuses on the Gospel of John's reference to Ahmad.

Core Idea
Gospel prophecies point to Islam's prophet, especially the name Ahmad in John.

This passage opens the discussion on how the Gospels, despite being Christian scripture, contain descriptions of the Prophet of Islam. The author lists the four canonical Gospels and mentions another Gospel called 'The Blessed Ahmad', as well as the Gospel of Barnabas which includes explicit mention of Muhammad. Rather than overwhelm us with all prophecies, the author wisely selects one key text from the Gospel of John for detailed examination.

Guided Path

The author treats these as supporting sources.

This shows a methodological choice for clarity.
4

The Paraclete Prophecy in John's Gospel
Jesus promises the Paraclete, interpreted as Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author interprets Jesus' promise of the Paraclete in John 14-16 as a prophecy referring to the Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
The Paraclete is not the Holy Spirit but a human prophet: Muhammad.

This lesson presents a key biblical passage that the author uses to argue for the prophethood of Muhammad. Jesus promises a 'Comforter' or 'Spirit of truth' who will come after him. The author contends that this figure is not the Holy Spirit but a human prophet, identified as Muhammad in Islamic tradition. Let's examine the text carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the Gospel passage
Read the Arabic and English translation of the passage from John 14-16. Note the repeated references to 'the Comforter' and 'Spirit of truth'.
2
Identify the key descriptions
List the roles and attributes of the Paraclete mentioned in the text: He will abide forever, teach all things, convict the world of sin, righteousness, and judgment, and speak what he hears.
These descriptions are used to distinguish the Paraclete from the Holy Spirit.
3

The author argues that these descriptions fit a human prophet like Muhammad, not a divine spirit. Focus on the phrase 'he will not speak on his own authority' – a mark of a prophet.
Compare with Quranic descriptions of Muhammad.
4
Reflect on the interfaith dimension

And I will pray the Father, and He will give you another Comforter, that He may abide with you forever— the Spirit of truth, whom the world cannot receive, because it neither sees Him nor knows Him; but you know Him, for He dwells with you and will be in you. (But the Comforter, the Holy Spirit, whom the Father will send in My name, He will teach you all things, and bring to your remembrance all things that I said to you.) It is to your advantage that I go away; for if I do not go away, the Helper will not come to you; but if I depart, I will send Him to you. And when He has come, He will convict the world of sin, and of righteousness, and of judgment: of sin, because they do not believe in Me; of righteousness, because I go to My Father and you see Me no more; of judgment, because the ruler of this world is judged. The author then left the quote with the reference. The context implies that this Paraclete is Muhammad, based on the name 'Ahmad' and the description of 'Spirit of truth' as a human prophet.

Prophecy of Muhammad in the Torah (Deuteronomy 33)
Explains the prophecy of Muhammad in Deuteronomy 33:1-3

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets a passage from Deuteronomy as a prophecy of Prophet Muhammad, identifying Paran as Mecca.

Core Idea
The Torah foretold the coming of Prophet Muhammad from Paran, which is Mecca.

This lesson examines a biblical text from Deuteronomy 33 that traditional Islamic scholarship interprets as a clear prophecy of Prophet Muhammad. Sanusi carefully unpacks each phrase—Sinai, Seir, and Paran—to show how the Torah itself points to the final prophet. As we read, consider how the author uses the Torah to support the claim that Muhammad's message abrogates previous laws.

Guided Path
1
Read the biblical quote and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the structure of the biblical verses cited and the author's introduction.
The passage begins with a quote from Deuteronomy 33:1-3.
2
Understand the author's interpretation of each location
The author explains three phrases: 'came from Sinai' (revelation to Moses), 'shone from Seir' (Jewish scholars in Palestine), and 'beamed from Mount Paran' (clear law from Paran). Focus on how each is linked to a phase of divine guidance.
Paran is the key term—it is identified as the mountains of Mecca.
3
Grasp the conclusion about abrogation
Read the final lines where the author argues that the companions of Muhammad will end the Jewish law irrevocably. Understand that this passage is used to prove that the Torah has been abrogated by Islam.
The author cites a Greek translation to support this.

Israel before his death. He said: 'The Lord came from Sinai. He shone upon them from Seir. He beamed from Mount Paran. He came from the ten thousands of holy ones, and at His right hand was a fiery law for them. He loved the people; all His holy ones are in Your hand. They sit at Your feet, receiving from Your words.' [Deuteronomy 33:1-3]. In this text we find the writer informing about the division of the blessing promised to Abraham, peace be upon him, according to what came from Moses, peace be upon him. He said: 'God came from Sinai,' meaning His law appeared at the hand of Moses on Mount Sinai. And by 'shining from Seir' he meant that the scholars of the Children of Israel used to interpret the Torah in the land of Palestine and Jordan. And by 'beaming from Mount Paran' he meant the appearance of a clear law from Paran. The evidence that Paran is the mountains of Mecca and that Paran is the homeland of the Children of Ishmael is what came in the Torah that the angel of God met Hagar and said to her: 'Get up, carry the boy and hold him with your hand, for I will make him a great nation... And God was with the boy, and he grew, and he lived in the wilderness, and he became a bowman. And he lived in the wilderness of Paran.' [Genesis 29]. And in some translations - the Greek - 'and with the ten thousands of the army of the leaders...' etc., meaning that the companions of the Prophet Muhammad will come to Palestine to end the Jewish law from it irrevocably. And whoever acts by it after his appearance, his deed will not be accepted by God. For God abrogated it at the hand of Muhammad, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage interprets a biblical text from Deuteronomy 33:1-3 as a prophecy of the Prophet Muhammad. The author first cites the text in which Moses speaks of God coming from Sinai, shining from Seir, and beaming from Mount Paran. The author explains that 'coming from Sinai' refers to the revelation of the Torah to Moses. 'Shining from Seir' refers to the Jewish scholars who later interpreted the Torah in Palestine and Jordan. 'Beaming from Mount Paran' is taken to mean the appearance of a clear law from Paran, which is identified as the mountains of Mecca, the homeland of the Ishmaelites. To support this identification, the author quotes Genesis 21 where Hagar and Ishmael live in the wilderness of Paran. The author then interprets a variant reading (the Greek translation) to mean that the companions of Prophet Muhammad will come to Palestine to abrogate the Jewish law. The conclusion is that acting according to the Torah after Muhammad's advent is invalid, as God abrogated it through him.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Paran refers to a place other than Mecca, such as a location in the Sinai Peninsula.
Correction: The author argues from the Torah itself that Paran is the mountains of Mecca, the homeland of the Children of Ishmael.

٢ - إن الأوصاف الواردة في النصر تدل على شخص بشري. ومن الأوصاف : أنه يبكت العالم ويخبر بكل شيء ويعلم كل شيء ويمجد المسيح ويرشد إلى جميع الحق ٣ ـ أن اليهود كانوا ينتظرون و النبي ، الذي نصت التوراة على مجيئه في زمان المسيح علي السلام . ولم يخبر المسبح أنه هو ، وقد أخبر يوحنا المعما. ان - الذي هو يحيى عليه السلام ـ بأنه سيأتي من بعده، بقوله : و يأتي بعدي من هو أقوى مني، الذي لست أهلا أن أنحني واحل سبور حذائه ، [ متى ٣] والذي يدل على أن اليهود كانوا ينتظرون هذا النبي زمان المسيح : من جاء في الأصحاح الأول من إنجيل يوحنا : أن اليهود من أورشليم أرسلوا وفداً من العلماء ليسألوا يحيى : هل أنت النبي ؟ هل أنت المسيح ؟ هل أنت إيلياء ؟ وأجاب يحيى لست المسيح ولست إيلياء ولست النبي . ثم نطق بقوله : : توبوا فقد اقترب ملكوت السموات ، ونطق بقوله : و يأتي بعدي من هو أقوى مني ... الخ ، ولقد نطق المسيح بمثل قوله فقد بدأ دعوته كما هو مبين في الأصحاح الثالث والرابع من إنجيل متى بقوله لبني إسرائيل : ه توبوا فقد اقترب ملكوت السموات ، كما يدل على تشابههما في الهدف من الدعوة ، وأنها معا يبشران محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
Preamble:
Second: The glad tidings of Islam in the Gospel
The holy Gospels according to the Christians are: the Gospel of Matthew, Mark, Luke, and John, and in these Gospels is the description of the Prophet of Islam. And there is a Gospel called the blessed Ahmad. And in the nineteenth century appeared a Gospel called the Gospel of Barnabas, and in it is the name of Muhammad and his descriptions. And it would make our discussion long if we mentioned all the prophetic texts from the Gospels. Therefore we will choose the text that refers to the name Ahmad in the Gospel of John.
The text:
In the fourteenth chapter of the Gospel of John and after it. Christ said to his disciples: 'If you love me, keep my commandments. And I will ask the Father, and He will give you another Comforter, to remain with you forever. The Spirit of truth, whom the world cannot receive because it neither sees Him nor knows Him. But you know Him, for He dwells with you and will be in you. (But the Comforter, the Holy Spirit, whom the Father will send in my name, He will teach you all things and remind you of everything I have told you.) And I have told you now before it happens, so that when it happens you may believe. But I tell you the truth: it is better for you that I go away. For if I do not go away, the Comforter will not come to you. But if I go, I will send Him to you. And when He comes, He will convict the world concerning sin and righteousness and judgment. Concerning sin, because they do not believe in me; concerning righteousness, because I am going to the Father and you will see me no longer; concerning judgment, because the ruler of this world is judged. I still have many things to say to you, but you cannot bear them now. But when the Spirit of truth comes, He will guide you into all truth, for He will not speak on His own authority, but whatever He hears He will speak, and He will declare to you the things that are to come. He will glorify me, for He will take what is mine and declare it to you.'
And the direction of the proof in this text:
1 - The word 'al-Mu'azzi' (the Comforter): 2 - The attributes mentioned in the text about the Comforter (with damma on the mim, fatha on the 'ayn, and shadda on the zay kasra). As for the word 'al-Mu'azzi', in the modern translations it is used, and it replaced in the old translations the word 'Baraklit' or 'Faraqlit' in some translations, meaning: the deputy of Christ who will come to console the Children of Israel in their loss of kingship and prophethood. So who is the Comforter? A - The Christians say it is the third god in the holy trinity. And they say that it came fifty days after the ascension of Christ. B - And the Muslims say that it is Muhammad, peace be upon him. And they support their statement with the following: 1 - The Christians and linguists say that the word 'Birkleit' is a Hebrew word meaning 'Ahmad'. It is translated in Greek as 'Birkleitos'. Since the Hebrew language had no vowel letters before the fifth century CE, it follows that Christ pronounced 'Bir Kliit' and not 'Bar Kliit'. This confirms that the Christians' view of the Comforter is false. For the Torah states that God is one, and likewise the Gospel states it. Therefore the statement of the Trinity is false. 2 - The attributes mentioned in the text indicate a human person. Among the attributes are: that he convicts the world, tells everything, knows everything, glorifies Christ, and guides to all truth. 3 - The Jews were waiting for the Prophet whose coming the Torah had foretold at the time of Christ, peace be upon him. Christ did not say that he himself was that prophet, but John the Baptist - who is Yahya, peace be upon him - said that he would come after him, saying: 'He who is coming after me is mightier than I, whose sandals I am not worthy to stoop down and untie.' [Matthew 3]. What indicates that the Jews were waiting for this prophet at the time of Christ is what came in the first chapter of the Gospel of John: that the Jews from Jerusalem sent a delegation of scholars to ask John: 'Are you the Prophet? Are you the Christ? Are you Elijah?' John answered: 'I am not the Christ, I am not Elijah, and I am not the Prophet.' Then he said: 'Repent, for the kingdom of heaven is at hand,' and he said: 'He who comes after me is mightier than I...' etc. And Christ spoke similarly when he began his mission, as shown in the third and fourth chapters of the Gospel of Matthew, saying to the Children of Israel: 'Repent, for the kingdom of heaven is at hand.' This indicates the similarity of their goal in the call, and that they both were giving glad tidings of Muhammad, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage presents the second set of glad tidings of Islam: the prophecy of Muhammad in the Gospel. The author first lists the four canonical Gospels and mentions the Gospel of Barnabas, then states that he will focus on the reference to 'Ahmad' in John's Gospel. He then quotes John 14:15-26 about the Paraclete (Comforter). After the citation, he analyzes the proof. First, he explains the Greek term 'Baraklit' (Paraclete) meaning 'deputy' or 'comforter'. He presents the Christian view that it is the Holy Spirit, and the Muslim view that it is Muhammad. The Muslim argument has three parts: (1) The Hebrew word underlying 'Paraclete' is 'Birkleit' meaning 'Ahmad', and since Hebrew lacked vowel letters, Christ would have said 'Bir Kliit' not 'Bar Kliit'; moreover, the Trinity is false because Scripture affirms God's oneness. (2) The attributes of the Paraclete in the text (e.g., convicting the world, telling everything, glorifying Christ) describe a human, not a divine being. (3) The Jews expected a prophet at that time, as shown by John the Baptist's denial of being the Christ or Elijah or the Prophet, and his announcement of one mightier coming after him. Christ's own preaching (repent, kingdom at hand) parallels John's, showing they both heralded Muhammad.

Arguments for Identifying the Paraclete as Muhammad
Presents three arguments that the Paraclete is Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three arguments Muslims use to prove that the Paraclete in John 14 is Prophet Muhammad: linguistic, attributes, and Jewish expectation.

Core Idea
Three arguments prove the Paraclete is Muhammad.

After citing John 14, the author analyzes the word 'Paraclete' and presents three rational arguments to support the Muslim identification. The first argument is linguistic: the underlying Hebrew word means 'Ahmad'. The second examines the attributes described, which fit a human prophet. The third refers to the Jewish expectation of a prophet at the time of Jesus, as shown by John the Baptist's testimony.

Guided Path
1
Read the linguistic argument
The author explains that the word 'Paraclete' in old translations is 'Baraklit' or 'Faraqlit', meaning deputy or comforter. He claims the Hebrew root is 'Birkleit' meaning 'Ahmad', and since Hebrew lacked vowel letters, Jesus would have said 'Bir Kliit' not 'Bar Kliit'. This refutes the Christian interpretation.
Also notes that the Trinity is false because Scripture affirms God's oneness.
2
Read the attributes argument
The attributes of the Paraclete described in the text (convicting the world, teaching all things, glorifying Christ) indicate a human person, not a divine spirit.
Consider how these attributes fit Muhammad's mission.
3
Read the Jewish expectation argument
The Jews awaited a prophet at the time of Jesus. John the Baptist denied being the Christ or Elijah or the Prophet, and announced one mightier coming after him. Jesus also began his mission with the same call to repentance as John, showing they both heralded Muhammad.
4
Reflect on the overall proof
Consider how these three arguments together support the claim that the Paraclete is Muhammad. The author concludes that the Christian view is false.

Commentary
This passage presents the second set of glad tidings of Islam: the prophecy of Muhammad in the Gospel. The author first lists the four canonical Gospels and mentions the Gospel of Barnabas, then states that he will focus on the reference to 'Ahmad' in John's Gospel. The Paraclete – Identity and Linguistic Evidence
Author defines al-Muʿazzī and presents linguistic proof that it refers to Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Muslim claim that the Paraclete is Muhammad and the linguistic argument from the Hebrew word 'Bīrklīt' meaning 'Ahmad'.

Core Idea
The Paraclete's original Hebrew name points to Ahmad (Muhammad), not the Holy Spirit.

This passage tackles a key interfaith debate: who is the Paraclete (al-Muʿazzī) prophesied in the Gospel? The author first clarifies the term and then presents the Muslim counter-argument to the Christian claim. We will focus on the definition of the term and the first proof—the linguistic argument that the Hebrew original of the Paraclete's name means 'Ahmad'.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and two views
Read the Arabic definition of al-Muʿazzī and the contrasting Christian and Muslim views. Note that Christians identify him as the Holy Spirit, Muslims as Muhammad.
The term 'al-Muʿazzī' translates 'the comforter' or 'paraclete'.
2
Understand the linguistic argument
Focus on the claim that the Hebrew word 'Bīrklīt' means 'Ahmad'. Understand that due to the absence of long vowels in early Hebrew, the original pronunciation was 'Bīr Klīt' (not 'Bār Klīt').
'Ahmad' is a name of the Prophet Muhammad meaning 'the praised one'.
3
Connect to the refutation of Trinity
Note how the linguistic point leads to a broader refutation of the Trinity, as both Torah and Gospel affirm God's oneness.
