ووجه الدليل في هذا النص . ١ - كلمة المعزي : بضم الميم وفتح العين وتشديد الزاي مكسورة - أما كلمة : المعزّي : فهي في التراجم الحديثة ، وموضع بدلها في التراجم القديمة كلمة ( باركيت ، أو فارقليط في بعض التراجم معناها : النائب عن المسيح الذي سيأتي ليعزي بني إسرائيل في فقدهم الملك والنبوة . فمن هو المعزي ؟ أ - يقول النصارى إنه الإله الثالث في الثالوث المقدس. ويقولون : إنه قد أتى بعد رفع المسيح إلى السماء بخمسين يوما ب - ويقول المسلمون : إنه محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم . ويستدلون على قولهم بما يلي : ١ - إن النصارى وعلياء اللغات يقولون إن كلمة ( بيركليت و كلمة عبرانية ومعناها : أحمد . وتترجم في اليونانية ( بيركليتوس ، وحيث أن اللغة العبرانية لم يكن فيها حروف مد قبل القرن الخامس الميلادي . فإذن يكون المسيح قد نطق ( بير كليت ، ولم ينطق ، بار كليت ، ويؤكد هذا أن وجهة نظر النصارى في ( المعزي ، وجهة باطلة . لأن التوراة نصت على أن الله واحد وكذلك نص الإنجيل . وعلى ذلك فالقول بالتثليث قول باطل . ٢ - إن الأوصاف الواردة في النص تدل على شخص بشري. ومن الأوصاف : أنه يبكت العالم ويخبر بكل شيء ويعلم كل شيء ويمجد المسيح ويرشد إلى جميع الحق ٣ ـ أن اليهود كانوا ينتظرون النبي ، الذي نصت التوراة على مجيئه في زمان المسيح عليه السلام . ولم يخبر المسيح أنه هو ، وقد أخبر يوحنا المعمدان - الذي هو يحيى عليه السلام ـ بأنه سيأتي من بعده، بقوله : و يأتي بعدي من هو أقوى مني، الذي لست أهلا أن أنحني وأحل سبور حذائه ، [ متى ٣] والذي يدل على أن اليهود كانوا ينتظرون هذا النبي زمان المسيح : من جاء في الأصحاح الأول من إنجيل يوحنا : أن اليهود من أورشليم أرسلوا وفداً من العلماء ليسألوا يحيى : هل أنت النبي ؟ هل أنت المسيح ؟ هل أنت إيلياء ؟ وأجاب يحيى لست المسيح ولست إيلياء ولست النبي . ثم نطق بقوله : توبوا فقد اقترب ملكوت السموات ، ونطق بقوله : و يأتي بعدي من هو أقوى مني ... الخ ، ولقد نطق المسيح بمثل قوله فقد بدأ دعوته كما هو مبين في الأصحاح الثالث والرابع من إنجيل متى بقوله لبني إسرائيل : توبوا فقد اقترب ملكوت السموات ، كما يدل على تشابههما في الهدف من الدعوة ، وأنهما معا يبشران محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
And the direction of the proof in this text. 1 - The word 'al-Muʿazzī': with ḍamma on the mīm, fatḥa on the ʿayn, and tashdīd on the zāy which is kasra. As for the word 'al-Muʿazzī', it is in modern translations, and its replacement in old translations is the word 'Bārkīt' or 'Fāraqliṭ' in some translations, meaning: the representative of Christ who will come to console the Children of Israel for their loss of kingship and prophethood. So who is al-Muʿazzī? A - The Christians say it is the third god in the Holy Trinity. And they say that he came fifty days after the raising of Christ to heaven. B - And the Muslims say that he is Muḥammad (peace be upon him). And they adduce for their statement the following: 1 - The Christians and the highest of languages say that the word 'Bīrklīt' is a Hebrew word and its meaning is 'Aḥmad'. And it is translated in Greek as 'Bīrklītūs'. And since the Hebrew language had no long vowels before the fifth century CE, then Christ must have pronounced 'Bīr Klīt' and not 'Bār Klīt'. And this confirms that the Christians' view concerning al-Muʿazzī is a false view, because the Torah stated that God is one, and likewise the Gospel stated it. Therefore, the statement of trinity is a false statement. 2 - The descriptions mentioned in the text indicate a human person. Among the descriptions: that he rebukes the world, informs of everything, knows everything, glorifies Christ, and guides to all truth. 3 - That the Jews were waiting for the Prophet whose coming the Torah had prescribed in the time of Christ (peace be upon him). Christ did not inform that he was him, and John the Baptist—who is Yaḥyā (peace be upon him)—informed that one would come after him, saying: 'After me comes one who is mightier than I, whose sandals I am not worthy to stoop and untie.' [Matthew 3] And which indicates that the Jews were waiting for this Prophet at the time of Christ: what came in the first chapter of the Gospel of John: that the Jews from Jerusalem sent a delegation of scholars to ask Yaḥyā: Are you the Prophet? Are you the Christ? Are you Elijah? And Yaḥyā answered: I am not the Christ, and I am not Elijah, and I am not the Prophet. Then he spoke saying: Repent, for the kingdom of heaven has drawn near, and he spoke saying: 'After me comes one who is mightier than I...' etc. And Christ spoke similarly when he began his call, as is shown in the third and fourth chapters of the Gospel of Matthew, saying to the Children of Israel: 'Repent, for the kingdom of heaven has drawn near.' And this indicates the similarity of their goals in the call, and that they together give glad tidings of Muḥammad (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument for the Muslim claim that the Paraclete (al-Muʿazzī) prophesied in the Bible is the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), not the Holy Spirit as Christians believe. The author first defines the term: 'al-Muʿazzī' in modern translations, replacing the older 'Bārkīt' or 'Fāraqliṭ', meaning the representative of Christ who consoles the Israelites. Then he presents the two views: Christians say it is the third person of the Trinity (the Holy Spirit) who came at Pentecost; Muslims say it is Muhammad. Three proofs are given: (1) Linguistic: The Hebrew word 'Bīrklīt' means 'Aḥmad' (the praised one), and since Hebrew had no long vowels before the 5th century, Christ must have said 'Bīr Klīt' (not 'Bār Klīt'), indicating Muhammad. Moreover, both Torah and Gospel affirm God's unity, so trinitarianism is false. (2) The descriptions of the Paraclete in the biblical text (rebuking the world, teaching all things, glorifying Christ) apply to a human being, not a divine person. (3) Historical expectation: The Jews in Jesus' time were awaiting a prophet besides the Messiah (John the Baptist was asked if he was the Prophet, Christ, or Elijah). John and Jesus both preached repentance and the coming kingdom, and their messages together point to Muhammad. The passage uses biblical citations to argue that Jesus and John foretold Muhammad.

Key Terms
معزي (al-Muʿazzī)
باركيت (Bārkīt)
فارقليط (Fāraqliṭ)
أحمد (Aḥmad)
بيركليت (Bīrklīt)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Paraclete is the Holy Spirit, a divine person.
Correction: Linguistic evidence shows the Hebrew original means 'Ahmad' (Muhammad), indicating a human prophet, not a divine being.

Checkpoint
What does the Hebrew word 'Bīrklīt' mean according to the author?
A) Comforter
B) Paraclete
C) Ahmad
D) Spirit of truth

Key Takeaway
The Hebrew origin of the Paraclete's name indicates it refers to Ahmad (Muhammad) rather than the Holy Spirit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Jesus himself foretold Muhammad by name through the Paraclete, what does that say about your response to the final prophet? Are you fully submitting to the evidence, or holding back due to cultural or social pressure?
?
Despite clear linguistic proof, many reject this truth. How does that challenge you to examine your own biases when encountering evidence that contradicts common beliefs?
?
Both Jews and Christians had scriptures pointing to Muhammad, yet most rejected him. When you encounter a truth that demands change, do you embrace it or find excuses? What is holding you back from complete conviction?

The Paraclete – Descriptions and Historical Expectation
Author presents descriptions and historical evidence that the Paraclete is a human prophet, Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second and third proofs that the Paraclete is Muhammad: the descriptions indicating a human prophet and the historical expectation of a prophet in Jesus' time.

Core Idea
The Paraclete's descriptions match a human prophet, and Jewish expectation of a coming prophet points to Muhammad.

After presenting the linguistic argument, the author provides two more proofs that the Paraclete is Muhammad. The second proof examines the biblical descriptions of the Paraclete, which indicate a human being, not a divine person. The third proof draws on the historical context: Jews were waiting for a prophet, and both John the Baptist and Jesus preached about a coming one, who is Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof: descriptions
Read the list of descriptions: rebukes the world, informs of everything, knows everything, glorifies Christ, guides to truth. Ask yourself: do these sound like a divine being or a human prophet?
The descriptions emphasize a teaching and guiding role, typical of a prophet.
2
Read the third proof: historical expectation
Read the biblical accounts: Jews asked John if he was the Prophet, Christ, or Elijah. John denied and pointed to a mightier one coming. Jesus also preached repentance and the kingdom. Both pointed forward to Muhammad.
Note the similarity between John's and Jesus' messages.
3
Synthesize the proofs
Combine the two proofs: the Paraclete must be human (proof 2) and was expected by Jews and foretold by John and Jesus (proof 3). Together they identify Muhammad.

The Objection: Miracles on a Liar's Hand
Objection and hypothetical reply about miracles on a liar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical form of the Ashʿarī objection: if God creates all actions, including false claims, He could manifest a miracle on a liar's hand, and the hypothetical reply that this would disable God.

Core Idea
If God creates everything, why can't He support a liar with a miracle?

In this lesson, we examine the opening objection of the passage. The objector argues that standard Ashʿarī theology—where God creates all actions, even disbelief—cannot consistently deny that God could show a miracle on a liar's hand. The objection then introduces a hypothetical reply that invoking necessity vs. proof leads to an impossibility. Understanding this sets the stage for the author's rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection's premise
Start with 'الأول : إن العجز...' and note the assumption that God creates all disbelief and ignorance. How does this undermine the claim that miracles cannot appear on a liar?
The objector is using the Ashʿarī's own thesis against them.
2
Follow the objection's conclusion
The objector concludes that if God creates ignorance, He can also do what leads to ignorance—i.e., show a miracle on a liar. Consider the implications for the proof of prophethood.
3
Examine the hypothetical reply
Read 'لا يقال : الدليل...' which argues that God can make us know truth by necessity, so He must also be able to do so by proof; otherwise miracles would be necessary. This reply tries to block the objection by showing it leads to disabling God.
This reply is not the author's own view; it's a potential rebuttal the objector anticipates.
4
Identify the structure
Notice the dialectical pattern: objection, then a hypothetical counter-argument. The author will later refute both. For now, grasp the logical flow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : إن العجز إنما يدل على صدق المدعى ، إذا اعتقدنا أنه لا يجوز ظهوره عقيب دعوى الكذاب . فمن اعتقد أنه لا خالق لجميع أنواع الكفر والفواحش إلا الله تعالى . فكيف يمكنه أن يقول : إنه لا يجوز من الله تعالى إظهار المعجز عقيب دعوى الكذاب ؟ بل نقول : إنه لا يفسده في إظهار المعجز عقيب دعوى الكذب ، إلا أن ذلك قد يؤدي إلى الجهل والتلبيس . فمن قال : إنه تعالى هو الخالق لكل كفر ، وكل جهل ابتداء . فكيف يمكنه أن يقول : إنه تعالى لا يجوز منه أن يفعل ما قد يؤدي إلى الجهل والتلبيس ؟ لا يقال : الدليل على أنه لا يجوز من الله تعالى إظهار المعجز على يد الكذاب : أنه تعالى قادر على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء عليهم السلام على سبيل الضرورة ، فوجب أيضاً أن يقدر على أن يعرفنا صدقهم بالدليل ، وإلا لزم المعجز . ثم إنه ثبت أنه لا دليل سوى المعجز ، فلو جوزنا من الله تعالى أن يظهر المعجز على يد الكاذب ، فحينئذ لزم أن لا يقدر الله تعالى على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء على سبيل الاستدلال . وذلك يفضي إلى تعجيز الله تعالى ، وأنه محال . لانا نقول : هذا الكلام ضعيف من وجوه : الأول : لا نسلم أنه تعالى لما قدر على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء على سبيل الاضطرار ، وجب أن يقدر على أن يعرفنا من صدقهم على سبيل الاستقلال . وما الجامع بينهما ؟ ثم إن القول بأن الله تعالى هو الخالق للكفر والفواحش ، يمتنع أن ينفي المعجز وجه دلالته على الصدق . والقادر إنما يكون قادراً على ما يكون في نفسه جائزاً صحيحاً ، لا على ما يكون في نفسه ممتنعاً . وليس كذلك تعريف صدقهم على سبيل الضرورة . لأن ذلك غير ممتنع في نفسه ، فصح كونه قادراً عليه . وظهر الفرق . الثاني : سلمنا أنه تعالى لما قدر على تعريف صدق الأنبياء اضطراراً ، وجب أن يقدر على تعريف صدقهم بالاكتساب . إلا أن مذهبكم يفضي إلى أن لا يقدر الله تعالى على ذلك ، فكان مذهبكم مفضياً إلى المحال ، فوجب أن يكون محالاً . وأنتم ما زدتم على هذا ، إلا السعي في إبطال مذهبكم . الثالث : إنكم قلتم : إنه لا يصح من الله تعالى إظهار المعجز على يد ...
First: Incapacity (al-ʿajz) only indicates the truthfulness of the claimant, if we believe that it is not permissible for it to appear in the wake of a liar's claim. So whoever believes that there is no creator of all types of disbelief and obscenities except God the Exalted—how can he say: 'It is not permissible from God the Exalted to manifest a miracle (al-muʿjiz) in the wake of a liar's claim?' Rather we say: He does not prevent Him from manifesting a miracle in the wake of a false claim, except that that may lead to ignorance and confusion. So whoever says that He the Exalted is the creator of every disbelief and every ignorance from the beginning—how can he say: 'It is not permissible from Him the Exalted to do what may lead to ignorance and confusion?' It is not said: The proof that it is not permissible from God the Exalted to manifest a miracle on the hand of a liar is that He the Exalted is able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets (peace be upon them) by necessity (ḍarūra), so it must also be that He is able to make us know their truthfulness by proof (dalīl), otherwise the miracle would be necessary. Then it is established that there is no proof except the miracle, so if we allow from God the Exalted that He manifest a miracle on the hand of a liar, then it would necessarily follow that God the Exalted is not able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by way of inference (istidlāl). That leads to disabling God the Exalted (taʿjīz), and that is impossible (muḥāl). But we say: This speech is weak in several respects: First: We do not concede that when He the Exalted is able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by way of compulsion (iḍṭirār), it is necessary that He be able to make us know their truthfulness by way of independence (istiqlāl). What is the common element between them? Moreover, the statement that God the Exalted is the creator of disbelief and obscenities prevents the miracle from negating its evidence for truthfulness. The capable (al-qādir) is only able to do what is in itself permissible and sound, not what is in itself impossible. It is not so with defining their truthfulness by way of necessity, because that is not impossible in itself, so it is valid that He is able to do it. And the difference becomes clear. Second: We concede that when He the Exalted is able to define the truthfulness of the prophets by compulsion, it must be that He is able to define their truthfulness by acquisition (iktisāb). However, your school of thought leads to the result that God the Exalted is not able to do that, so your school of thought leads to what is impossible, so it must be impossible. You have added nothing to this except striving to invalidate your own school. Third: You said: It is not valid from God the Exalted to manifest a miracle on the hand...
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection regarding the proof of prophethood through miracles. The objection states that if one believes God creates all disbelief and evil, then there is no reason why He could not manifest a miracle on a liar's hand, thereby making miracles an unreliable proof. The author first presents the objection (the 'First' point) that if God creates all disbelief, the critic cannot consistently claim that God would not show a miracle on a liar's hand, because He could, and that would lead to ignorance. Then the objection continues: how can one say God cannot do something that leads to ignorance if He is the creator of ignorance? Then a hypothetical reply is given: someone might argue that proof that God does not show a miracle on a liar's hand is that He can make us know the truth of prophets by necessity (ḍarūra), so He must also be able to make us know by proof; otherwise miracle would be necessary. And since only miracles serve as proof, allowing miracles on a liar's hand would imply God cannot make us know truth by inference, disabling God—impossible. Then the author responds with three rebuttals (the 'lāna naqūl' section). First: the claim that ability to know by necessity entails ability to know by proof is not conceded; there is no common element. Moreover, the view that God creates disbelief and evil does not negate that a miracle is evidence of truth; the capable can do what is possible in itself, and defining truth by necessity is possible, so the analogy fails. Second: even if we grant the necessity, the opponent's own view that God creates disbelief leads to the impossibility of God defining truth by acquisition, so their view leads to impossibility and is self-refuting. Third: (cut off) they said it is not valid for God to show a miracle on the hand of a liar. The passage demonstrates a typical kalam dialectical argument, emphasizing that divine power (qudra) is limited only by logical possibility, and that the proof of miracles remains valid even if God creates all actions.

Key Terms
عجز (ʿajz)
صدق (ṣidq)
تعجيز (taʿjīz)
اضطرار (iḍṭirār)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that Ashʿarī theology cannot defend miracles because God creates all actions.
Correction: This objection is precisely the challenge the author addresses; the passage shows that the objection is recognized and refuted.

Checkpoint
What is the core premise used by the objector to challenge the exclusivity of miracles?
A) God does not create disbelief.
B) God creates all types of disbelief and ignorance.
C) Miracles are not possible on a liar's hand.
D) The prophets were truthful.

Key Takeaway
The objection uses the Ashʿarī commitment to God creating all actions to argue that miracles cannot be exclusive proof of truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the evidence for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him), does your trust rest more on the miracle of the Quran itself or on a prior conviction that God would not allow a liar to perform such a miracle? Which of these is stronger in your heart, and why?

Three Rebuttals: Defending Miracle Evidence
Author's three rebuttals to the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's three rebuttals to the objection, focusing on the distinction between knowledge by necessity and by proof, and the self-refuting nature of the opponent's position.

Core Idea
The opponent's own view that God creates all disbelief actually refutes their objection.

After presenting the objection and a hypothetical reply, the author now delivers three rebuttals. The first rebuttal denies the logical link between knowledge by necessity and knowledge by proof, and clarifies the scope of divine power. The second rebuttal shows that the opponent's position leads to an impossibility. The third rebuttal is cut off but likely continues the argument. This lesson examines these refutations in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the first rebuttal
Start with 'لانا نقول : هذا الكلام ضعيف من وجوه : الأول : لا نسلم...' and identify why the author rejects the analogy between knowledge by necessity and knowledge by proof.
The author distinguishes between what is logically possible (jāʾiz ṣaḥīḥ) and what is impossible (mumtaniʿ).
2
Analyze the second rebuttal
Read the second rebuttal: 'الثاني : سلمنا أنه تعالى لما قدر...' and understand how the author turns the opponent's argument against them.
Even if we concede the premise, the opponent's own doctrine (that God creates all acts) leads to the very impossibility they warned against.
3
Examine the third rebuttal (partial)
Read the beginning of the third rebuttal: 'الثالث : إنكم قلتم : إنه لا يصح من الله تعالى...' and note it is incomplete. Try to infer what the author might be arguing.
The argument likely continues to show that the opponent's claim that God cannot show a miracle on a liar is inconsistent with their own principles.
4
Synthesize the overall strategy
Consider how the three rebuttals work together: the first denies the assumed connection, the second shows self-refutation, and the third (likely) highlights an inconsistency.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection regarding the proof of prophethood through miracles. The objection states that if one believes God creates all disbelief and evil, then there is no reason why He could not manifest a miracle on a liar's hand, thereby making miracles an unreliable proof. The author first presents the objection (the 'First' point) that if God creates all disbelief, the critic cannot consistently claim that God would not show a miracle on a liar's hand, because He could, and that would lead to ignorance. Then the objection continues: how can one say God cannot do something that leads to ignorance if He is the creator of ignorance? Then a hypothetical reply is given: someone might argue that proof that God does not show a miracle on a liar's hand is that He can make us know the truth of prophets by necessity (ḍarūra), so He must also be able to make us know by proof; otherwise miracle would be necessary. And since only miracles serve as proof, allowing miracles on a liar's hand would imply God cannot make us know truth by inference, disabling God—impossible. Then the author responds with three rebuttals (the 'lāna naqūl' section). First: the claim that ability to know by necessity entails ability to know by proof is not conceded; there is no common element. Moreover, the view that God creates disbelief and evil does not negate that a miracle is evidence of truth; the capable can do what is possible in itself, and defining truth by necessity is possible, so the analogy fails. Second: even if we grant the necessity, the opponent's own view that God creates disbelief leads to the impossibility of God defining truth by acquisition, so their view leads to impossibility and is self-refuting. Third: (cut off) they said it is not valid for God to show a miracle on the hand of a liar. The passage demonstrates a typical kalam dialectical argument, emphasizing that divine power (qudra) is limited only by logical possibility, and that the proof of miracles remains valid even if God creates all actions.

Correction: The author affirms that God is powerful only over what is intrinsically possible, which preserves the proof of miracles.

The Objection Against Miracles on Liars
Objection that miracles on liars entail divine incapacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational objection that permitting miracles on liars would imply divine incapacity to make us know prophets by inference.

Core Idea
If God can give necessary knowledge, He must also give inferential knowledge; otherwise miracles on liars prove incapacity.

Before the author gives his rebuttals, he presents the opponent's argument in its strongest form. The objection turns on a comparison between two types of knowledge: necessary and inferential. Understanding this objection is essential to appreciate the refutation that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Identify the main claim: that God must be able to make us know prophets by inference because He can by necessity.
The objector uses a logical 'otherwise' clause to link miracles on liars to divine incapacity.
2
Trace the argument
Notice the steps: (1) God can give necessary knowledge, (2) so He must also give inferential knowledge, (3) the only evidence is miracles, (4) if miracles can appear on liars, then inferential knowledge becomes impossible, (5) that would make God incapable.
Step (3) is key: it assumes miracles are the only evidence for truthfulness.
3
Consider the conclusion
The objector claims that the Ash'ari view leads to an impossibility (divine incapacity). Ask yourself: what assumption underlies this conclusion?
The objector assumes that necessary and inferential knowledge are analogous in possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمكنه أن يقول : إنه تعالى لا يجوز منه أن يفعل ما قد يؤدي إلى الجهل والتلبيس ؟ لا يقال : الدليل على أنه لا يجوز من الله تعالى إظهار المعجز على يد الكذاب : أنه تعالى قادر على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء عليهم السلام على سبيل الضرورة ، فوجب أيضاً أن يقدر على أن يعرفنا صدقهم بالدليل ، وإلا لزم المعجز . ثم إنه ثبت أنه لا دليل سوى المعجز ، فلو جوزنا من الله تعالى أن يظهر المعجز على يد الكاذب، فحينئذ لزم أن لا يقدر الله تعالى على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء على سبيل الاستدلال . وذلك يفضي إلى تعجيز الله تعالى ، وأنه محال لانا نقول : هذا الكلام ضعيف من وجوه : الأول : لا نسلم أنه تعالى لما قدر على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء على سبيل الاضطرار ، وجب أن يقدر على أن يعرفنا من صدقهم على سبيل الاستقلال [؟] . وما الجامع بينهما ؟ ثم إن القول بأن الله تعالى هو الخالق للكفر والفواحش ، يمتنع أن ينفي المعجز وجه دلالته على الصدق . والقادر إنما يكون قادراً على ما يكون في نفسه جائزاً صحيحاً ، لا على ما يكون في نفسه ممتنعاً . وليس كذلك تعريف صدقهم على سبيل الضرورة . لأن ذلك غير ممتنع في نفسه ، فصح كونه قادراً عليه . وظهر الفرق الثاني : سلمنا أنه تعالى لما قدر على تعريف صدق الأنبياء اضطراراً ، وجب أن يقدر على تعريف صدقهم بالاكتساب . إلا أن مذهبكم يفضي إلى أن لا يقدر الله تعالى على ذلك ، فكان مذهبكم مفضياً إلى المحال ، فوجب أن يكون محالاً. وأنتم ما زدتم على هذا ، إلا السعي في إبطال مذهبكم . الثالث : إنكم قلتم : إنه لا يصح من الله تعالى إظهار المعجز على يد الكاذب ، وإلا لزم تعجيزه على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء بالاكتساب . ونحن نقول : وجب أن لا يصح من الله تعريفنا صدق الأنبياء بالاكتساب ، وإلا لزم تعجيزه عن خلق المعجزات عقيب دعوى الكذاب . ولما كان ممتنعاً في نفسه ، لم يكن عدم القدرة عليه عجزاً . قلنا : ولم ينفصلون عمن يقول : دلالة المعجز على الصدق ، لما كانت ممتنعة لنفسها ، لم يكن عدم القدرة على خلق هذا الدليل : عجزاً ؟ وبالجملة : فلا فرق بين الجانبين الرابع : وهو أن قولكم : إنه تعالى لا يصح منه خلق المعجز عقيب دعوى الكاذب : كلام باطل . لأن فلق القمر عقيب تكلم إنسان بكلام كذب ممكن في نفسه . والله تعالى قادر على كل الممكنات ، فيمتنع حصول هذا الامتناع نظرا إلى القدرة ، ويمتنع أيضاً حصوله نظراً إلى الداعي . لأن قبح القبائح لا تأثير لها عندكم في هذا الباب . ولما ثبت أنه لا يمكن القول بحصول هذا الامتناع لا نظراً إلى القدرة ولا نظراً إلى الإرادة والداعي كان القول بثبوت هذا الامتناع باطلاً قطعاً
He might say: It is not permissible for Him, Exalted, to do what might lead to ignorance and confusion? It is not said: The proof that it is not permissible for God to show a miracle at the hand of a liar is that He, Exalted, is able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets, peace be upon them, by necessity, so He must also be able to make us know their truthfulness by evidence, otherwise a miracle would be necessary. Then it is established that there is no evidence besides the miracle, so if we permit God to show a miracle at the hand of the liar, then it would follow that God is not able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by inference. And that leads to incapacitating God, and that is impossible. We say: This speech is weak in several respects: First: We do not accept that when He, Exalted, is able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by necessity, He must be able to make us know their truthfulness by inference[؟]. And what is the commonality between them? Then the statement that God is the creator of unbelief and abominations prevents the miracle from negating its indication of truthfulness. The capable is only capable of what is in itself permissible and sound, not of what is in itself impossible. And the definition of their truthfulness by necessity is not like that, because that is not impossible in itself, so it is correct that He is capable of it. And the difference is clear. Second: We grant that when He, Exalted, is able to define the truthfulness of the prophets by necessity, He must be able to define their truthfulness by acquisition. But your doctrine leads to God not being able to do that, so your doctrine leads to absurdity, so it must be absurd. And you have not added to this except striving to invalidate your doctrine. Third: You said: It is not correct for God to show a miracle at the hand of the liar, otherwise it would necessitate incapacitating Him to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by acquisition. And we say: It must not be correct for God to define for us the truthfulness of the prophets by acquisition, otherwise it would necessitate incapacitating Him from creating miracles after the claim of the liar. And since it is impossible in itself, the lack of power over it is not incapacity. We said: And they do not separate from the one who says: The indication of the miracle of truthfulness, since it is impossible in itself, the lack of power to create this evidence is not incapacity? In summary: So there is no difference between the two sides. Fourth: And that your statement: It is not correct for God to create a miracle after the claim of the liar is false speech. Because splitting the moon after a person speaks a lie is possible in itself. And God is capable of all possibles, so it is impossible for this impossibility to occur, with regard to power, and it is also impossible for it to occur with regard to the motive. Because the ugliness of ugly deeds has no effect with you in this matter. And since it is established that it is not possible to claim the occurrence of this impossibility, neither with regard to power nor with regard to will and motive, the claim of the existence of this impossibility is absolutely false.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the Ash'ari view that God alone creates actions and that miracles are signs of truthfulness. The objector argues that if God can make us know prophets necessarily, He should also be able to make us know through evidence; otherwise, showing a miracle on a liar would mean God cannot make us know, implying incapacity. The author refutes this in four points. (1) The two types of knowledge are distinct: necessary knowledge is possible but inferential knowledge may not be due to intrinsic impossibility. The claim that God is creator of actions does not undermine the miracle's indication. (2) Even if we accept the premise, the opponent's own view leads to the same absurdity, thus it is self-defeating. (3) The opponent's argument is symmetric; if showing a miracle on a liar implies incapacity, then not showing it also implies incapacity, so no difference. (4) It is impossible for God to be incapable of creating a miracle after a liar's claim because splitting the moon is possible, and God is powerful over all possibles; there is no impediment in power or will since evil does not affect divine will. Thus the claim of impossibility is false.

Key Terms
معجز
صدق الأنبياء
تعجيز
اضطرار
اكتساب

C) Prophets would no longer be necessary.
D) The liar would become truthful.

Key Takeaway
The objection uses a comparison between necessary and inferential knowledge to argue that divine power would be limited if miracles could appear on liars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely more on immediate certainty (like necessary knowledge) or on reasoned evidence in your faith? Which does this passage suggest is more reliable, and which does your soul actually lean on? What will you do today to strengthen the weaker one?
?
If you had to prove to yourself that a prophet is truthful without relying on a miracle, could you? Or would you demand a shortcut? This lesson shows that even the evidence of miracles requires logical reasoning. Have you ever taken the time to examine the rational basis of your own belief in the Prophet ﷺ? If not, what stops you?
?
This argument exposes that doubting the link between miracles and truthfulness leads to questioning God's power. Could your casual acceptance of signs (or lack thereof) in your life be a form of intellectual laziness that indirectly questions His perfect ability? What step will you take this week to study one evidence of prophethood more deeply?

First Rebuttal: Distinct Types of Knowledge
First rebuttal: Denies equivalence between necessary and inferential knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first rebuttal: necessary and inferential knowledge are distinct categories, and the latter may be intrinsically impossible.

Core Idea
Necessary knowledge and inferential knowledge are not comparable; only possible things are within divine power.

The author begins his refutation by denying the equivalence assumed in the objection. He argues that God's ability to give necessary knowledge does not imply ability to give inferential knowledge, because the latter may be impossible in itself. He also clarifies that the miracle's evidential force is not nullified by God's creation of unbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the first rebuttal
Read the Arabic and translation, noting how the author rejects the premise that necessary knowledge implies inferential knowledge.
The key word 'الاستقلال' may be a manuscript error for 'الاستدلال' (inference).
2
Understand the distinction
The author argues that capability applies only to what is intrinsically possible. Necessary knowledge is possible; inferential knowledge (through miracles) may be impossible because it depends on a correspondence between miracle and truthfulness that cannot be established if God creates unbelief.
The author implies that the miracle's indication of truthfulness is an intrinsic property, not something God can arbitrarily create.
3
See the conclusion
Since there is no commonality between the two types of knowledge, the objector's argument fails. The difference is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمكنه أن يقول : إنه تعالى لا يجوز منه أن يفعل ما قد يؤدي إلى الجهل والتلبيس ؟ لا يقال : الدليل على أنه لا يجوز من الله تعالى إظهار المعجز على يد الكذاب : أنه تعالى قادر على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء عليهم السلام على سبيل الضرورة ، فوجب أيضاً أن يقدر على أن يعرفنا صدقهم بالدليل ، وإلا لزم المعجز . ثم إنه ثبت أنه لا دليل سوى المعجز ، فلو جوزنا من الله تعالى أن يظهر المعجز على يد الكاذب، فحينئذ لزم أن لا يقدر الله تعالى على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء على سبيل الاستدلال . وذلك يفضي إلى تعجيز الله تعالى ، وأنه محال لانا نقول : هذا الكلام ضعيف من وجوه : الأول : لا نسلم أنه تعالى لما قدر على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء على سبيل الاضطرار ، وجب أن يقدر على أن يعرفنا من صدقهم على سبيل الاستقلال [؟] . وما الجامع بينهما ؟ ثم إن القول بأن الله تعالى هو الخالق للكفر والفواحش ، يمتنع أن ينفي المعجز وجه دلالته على الصدق . والقادر إنما يكون قادراً على ما يكون في نفسه جائزاً صحيحاً ، لا على ما يكون في نفسه ممتنعاً . وليس كذلك تعريف صدقهم على سبيل الضرورة . لأن ذلك غير ممتنع في نفسه ، فصح كونه قادراً عليه . وظهر الفرق الثاني : سلمنا أنه تعالى لما قدر على تعريف صدق الأنبياء اضطراراً ، وجب أن يقدر على تعريف صدقهم بالاكتساب . إلا أن مذهبكم يفضي إلى أن لا يقدر الله تعالى على ذلك ، فكان مذهبكم مفضياً إلى المحال ، فوجب أن يكون محالاً. وأنتم ما زدتم على هذا ، إلا السعي في إبطال مذهبكم . الثالث : إنكم قلتم : إنه لا يصح من الله تعالى إظهار المعجز على يد الكاذب ، وإلا لزم تعجيزه على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء بالاكتساب . ونحن نقول : وجب أن لا يصح من الله تعريفنا صدق الأنبياء بالاكتساب ، وإلا لزم تعجيزه عن خلق المعجزات عقيب دعوى الكذاب . ولما كان ممتنعاً في نفسه ، لم يكن عدم القدرة عليه عجزاً . قلنا : ولم ينفصلون عمن يقول : دلالة المعجز على الصدق ، لما كانت ممتنعة لنفسها ، لم يكن عدم القدرة على خلق هذا الدليل : عجزاً ؟ وبالجملة : فلا فرق بين الجانبين الرابع : وهو أن قولكم : إنه تعالى لا يصح منه خلق المعجز عقيب دعوى الكاذب : كلام باطل . لأن فلق القمر عقيب تكلم إنسان بكلام كذب ممكن في نفسه . والله تعالى قادر على كل الممكنات ، فيمتنع حصول هذا الامتناع نظرا إلى القدرة ، ويمتنع أيضاً حصوله نظراً إلى الداعي . لأن قبح القبائح لا تأثير لها عندكم في هذا الباب . ولما ثبت أنه لا يمكن القول بحصول هذا الامتناع لا نظراً إلى القدرة ولا نظراً إلى الإرادة والداعي كان القول بثبوت هذا الامتناع باطلاً قطعاً
He might say: It is not permissible for Him, Exalted, to do what might lead to ignorance and confusion? It is not said: The proof that it is not permissible for God to show a miracle at the hand of a liar is that He, Exalted, is able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets, peace be upon them, by necessity, so He must also be able to make us know their truthfulness by evidence, otherwise a miracle would be necessary. Then it is established that there is no evidence besides the miracle, so if we permit God to show a miracle at the hand of the liar, then it would follow that God is not able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by inference. And that leads to incapacitating God, and that is impossible. We say: This speech is weak in several respects: First: We do not accept that when He, Exalted, is able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by necessity, He must be able to make us know their truthfulness by inference[؟]. And what is the commonality between them? Then the statement that God is the creator of unbelief and abominations prevents the miracle from negating its indication of truthfulness. The capable is only capable of what is in itself permissible and sound, not of what is in itself impossible. And the definition of their truthfulness by necessity is not like that, because that is not impossible in itself, so it is correct that He is capable of it. And the difference is clear. Second: We grant that when He, Exalted, is able to define the truthfulness of the prophets by necessity, He must be able to define their truthfulness by acquisition. But your doctrine leads to God not being able to do that, so your doctrine leads to absurdity, so it must be absurd. And you have not added to this except striving to invalidate your doctrine. Third: You said: It is not correct for God to show a miracle at the hand of the liar, otherwise it would necessitate incapacitating Him to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by acquisition. And we say: It must not be correct for God to define for us the truthfulness of the prophets by acquisition, otherwise it would necessitate incapacitating Him from creating miracles after the claim of the liar. And since it is impossible in itself, the lack of power over it is not incapacity. We said: And they do not separate from the one who says: The indication of the miracle of truthfulness, since it is impossible in itself, the lack of power to create this evidence is not incapacity? In summary: So there is no difference between the two sides. Fourth: And that your statement: It is not correct for God to create a miracle after the claim of the liar is false speech. Because splitting the moon after a person speaks a lie is possible in itself. And God is capable of all possibles, so it is impossible for this impossibility to occur, with regard to power, and it is also impossible for it to occur with regard to the motive. Because the ugliness of ugly deeds has no effect with you in this matter. And since it is established that it is not possible to claim the occurrence of this impossibility, neither with regard to power nor with regard to will and motive, the claim of the existence of this impossibility is absolutely false.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the Ash'ari view that God alone creates actions and that miracles are signs of truthfulness. The objector argues that if God can make us know prophets necessarily, He should also be able to make us know through evidence; otherwise, showing a miracle on a liar would mean God cannot make us know, implying incapacity. The author refutes this in four points. (1) The two types of knowledge are distinct: necessary knowledge is possible but inferential knowledge may not be due to intrinsic impossibility. The claim that God is creator of actions does not undermine the miracle's indication. (2) Even if we accept the premise, the opponent's own view leads to the same absurdity, thus it is self-defeating. (3) The opponent's argument is symmetric; if showing a miracle on a liar implies incapacity, then not showing it also implies incapacity, so no difference. (4) It is impossible for God to be incapable of creating a miracle after a liar's claim because splitting the moon is possible, and God is powerful over all possibles; there is no impediment in power or will since evil does not affect divine will. Thus the claim of impossibility is false.

Key Terms
اضطرار
اكتساب
استقلال
دلالة
قادر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the miracle's indication of truthfulness?
A) It is negated by God's creation of unbelief.
B) It remains despite God being the creator of unbelief.
C) It only works if the miracle is from a prophet.
D) It depends on the observer's intention.

Key Takeaway
The first rebuttal establishes that necessary and inferential knowledge are not comparable, and the miracle retains its evidential force independently.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate the evidences for your faith, do you rely more on 'necessary' certainties (like the feeling of truth) or on 'inferential' proofs (like arguments from miracles)? Which one is more secure, and which one do you actually lean on in moments of doubt? Be honest.
?
The author argues that even if God creates unbelief, the miracle still points to truth. Is there an area in your life where you have allowed the existence of evil or disbelief to weaken your trust in the clear signs of Allah? What would it take to restore that trust today?
?
The distinction between what is possible and impossible per se is not just an abstract principle—it defines the limits of what you should expect from Allah. Have you ever demanded something from Allah that is actually impossible in itself, and then felt disappointed when it didn't happen? How can this lesson recalibrate your expectations and deepen your reliance on His wisdom?

Second Rebuttal: Self-Defeating Argument
Second rebuttal: Opponent's argument is self-defeating.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second rebuttal: the opponent's own argument leads to the same absurdity it tries to avoid.

Core Idea
The opponent's doctrine implies divine incapacity no less than the Ash'ari view, making it self-defeating.

The author now grants the opponent's premise for the sake of argument, but shows that it backfires. If God must be able to define truthfulness by acquisition, then the opponent's own denial of miracles on liars would imply that God cannot do so, leading to the very absurdity they accused the Ash'aris of.

Guided Path
1
Read the second rebuttal
Read the passage and translation. Notice that the author starts with 'We grant' (سلمنا), temporarily accepting the opponent's logic.
This is a common dialectical move: assuming the opponent's premise to show it leads to a contradiction.
2
Trace the logic
If God must be able to define truthfulness by acquisition, and the opponent's doctrine denies that miracles can appear on liars (the only evidence), then the opponent's doctrine implies that God cannot define truthfulness by acquisition. That is a contradiction.
Thus the opponent's view is self-refuting.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that the opponent's doctrine leads to absurdity, so the opponent has only succeeded in invalidating their own position.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The opponent's argument is logically consistent.
Correction: The author shows that the opponent's own premise leads to a contradiction, so the argument is not consistent.

Checkpoint
What does the author claim the opponent's doctrine leads to?
A) Necessary knowledge of prophets.

D) Acceptance of miracles on liars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The opponent thought they were defending God's power, but their view actually limited it. Consider a conviction you hold about Islam that you have never critically examined. Could it be that your belief, despite good intentions, actually restricts God's ability to act in ways you haven't considered? Are you willing to test that conviction against the sources, even if it feels uncomfortable?
?
This argument shows that inconsistency in one's position leads to self-defeat. In what area of your life—your character, your worship, or your relationships—are you demanding consistency from others but excusing your own contradictions? How will you address that gap starting today?
?
The author turns the opponent's logic against them. Is there an argument you use against other Muslims or non-Muslims that could be turned back on you? Write down one such argument you have used, and then honestly examine whether you live consistently with it.

Third and Fourth Rebuttals: Symmetry and Possibility of Miracles
Third and fourth rebuttals: symmetry and the possibility of a miracle on a liar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third and fourth rebuttals: the opponent's argument is symmetric and the occurrence of a miracle on a liar is intrinsically possible.

Core Idea
The opponent's argument is symmetric, and a miracle on a liar is not impossible—only God's power and will decide.

The author delivers two final rebuttals. First, he exposes a symmetry: the opponent's reasoning applies equally to their own view, so no side can claim advantage. Second, he argues that there is no intrinsic impossibility in a miracle occurring at the hand of a liar, using the example of the splitting of the moon. The only limitations are divine power and will, and neither is affected by the moral quality of the claimant.

Guided Path
1
Read the third rebuttal
Read the text about the symmetrical argument. The author shows that if one view leads to incapacity, the other does as well.
The symmetry point is a devastating rhetorical move: it neutralizes the opponent's main objection.
2
Read the fourth rebuttal
Read the fourth point. The author gives a concrete example: splitting the moon after a liar's claim is possible in itself.
This example illustrates that the impossibility is not in the act itself but in the opponent's assumption.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes that the opponent's claim of impossibility is absolutely false, because there is no impediment in power or in divine will (since God is not swayed by the ugliness of deeds).

صدق الأنبياء على سبيل الاضطرار ، وجب أن يقدر على أن يعرفنا من صدقهم على سبيل الاستقلال [؟] . وما الجامع بينهما ؟ ثم إن القول بأن الله تعالى هو الخالق للكفر والفواحش ، يمتنع أن ينفي المعجز وجه دلالته على الصدق . والقادر إنما يكون قادراً على ما يكون في نفسه جائزاً صحيحاً ، لا على ما يكون في نفسه ممتنعاً . وليس كذلك تعريف صدقهم على سبيل الضرورة . لأن ذلك غير ممتنع في نفسه ، فصح كونه قادراً عليه . وظهر الفرق الثاني : سلمنا أنه تعالى لما قدر على تعريف صدق الأنبياء اضطراراً ، وجب أن يقدر على تعريف صدقهم بالاكتساب . إلا أن مذهبكم يفضي إلى أن لا يقدر الله تعالى على ذلك ، فكان مذهبكم مفضياً إلى المحال ، فوجب أن يكون محالاً. وأنتم ما زدتم على هذا ، إلا السعي في إبطال مذهبكم . الثالث : إنكم قلتم : إنه لا يصح من الله تعالى إظهار المعجز على يد الكاذب ، وإلا لزم تعجيزه على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء بالاكتساب . ونحن نقول : وجب أن لا يصح من الله تعريفنا صدق الأنبياء بالاكتساب ، وإلا لزم تعجيزه عن خلق المعجزات عقيب دعوى الكذاب . ولما كان ممتنعاً في نفسه ، لم يكن عدم القدرة عليه عجزاً . قلنا : ولم ينفصلون عمن يقول : دلالة المعجز على الصدق ، لما كانت ممتنعة لنفسها ، لم يكن عدم القدرة على خلق هذا الدليل : عجزاً ؟ وبالجملة : فلا فرق بين الجانبين الرابع : وهو أن قولكم : إنه تعالى لا يصح منه خلق المعجز عقيب دعوى الكاذب : كلام باطل . لأن فلق القمر عقيب تكلم إنسان بكلام كذب ممكن في نفسه . والله تعالى قادر على كل الممكنات ، فيمتنع حصول هذا الامتناع نظرا إلى القدرة ، ويمتنع أيضاً حصوله نظراً إلى الداعي . لأن قبح القبائح لا تأثير لها عندكم في هذا الباب . ولما ثبت أنه لا يمكن القول بحصول هذا الامتناع لا نظراً إلى القدرة ولا نظراً إلى الإرادة والداعي كان القول بثبوت هذا الامتناع باطلاً قطعاً
He might say: It is not permissible for Him, Exalted, to do what might lead to ignorance and confusion? It is not said: The proof that it is not permissible for God to show a miracle at the hand of a liar is that He, Exalted, is able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets, peace be upon them, by necessity, so He must also be able to make us know their truthfulness by evidence, otherwise a miracle would be necessary. Then it is established that there is no evidence besides the miracle, so if we permit God to show a miracle at the hand of the liar, then it would follow that God is not able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by inference. And that leads to incapacitating God, and that is impossible. We say: This speech is weak in several respects: First: We do not accept that when He, Exalted, is able to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by necessity, He must be able to make us know their truthfulness by inference[؟]. And what is the commonality between them? Then the statement that God is the creator of unbelief and abominations prevents the miracle from negating its indication of truthfulness. The capable is only capable of what is in itself permissible and sound, not of what is in itself impossible. And the definition of their truthfulness by necessity is not like that, because that is not impossible in itself, so it is correct that He is capable of it. And the difference is clear. Second: We grant that when He, Exalted, is able to define the truthfulness of the prophets by necessity, He must be able to define their truthfulness by acquisition. But your doctrine leads to God not being able to do that, so your doctrine leads to absurdity, so it must be absurd. And you have not added to this except striving to invalidate your doctrine. Third: You said: It is not correct for God to show a miracle at the hand of the liar, otherwise it would necessitate incapacitating Him to make us know the truthfulness of the prophets by acquisition. And we say: It must not be correct for God to define for us the truthfulness of the prophets by acquisition, otherwise it would necessitate incapacitating Him from creating miracles after the claim of the liar. And since it is impossible in itself, the lack of power over it is not incapacity. We said: And they do not separate from the one who says: The indication of the miracle of truthfulness, since it is impossible in itself, the lack of power to create this evidence is not incapacity? In summary: So there is no difference between the two sides. Fourth: And that your statement: It is not correct for God to create a miracle after the claim of the liar is false speech. Because splitting the moon after a person speaks a lie is possible in itself. And God is capable of all possibles, so it is impossible for this impossibility to occur, with regard to power, and it is also impossible for it to occur with regard to the motive. Because the ugliness of ugly deeds has no effect with you in this matter. And since it is established that it is not possible to claim the occurrence of this impossibility, neither with regard to power nor with regard to will and motive, the claim of the existence of this impossibility is absolutely false.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the Ash'ari view that God alone creates actions and that miracles are signs of truthfulness. The objector argues that if God can make us know prophets necessarily, He should also be able to make us know through evidence; otherwise, showing a miracle on a liar would mean God cannot make us know, implying incapacity. The author refutes this in four points. (1) The two types of knowledge are distinct: necessary knowledge is possible but inferential knowledge may not be due to intrinsic impossibility. The claim that God is creator of actions does not undermine the miracle's indication. (2) Even if we accept the premise, the opponent's own view leads to the same absurdity, thus it is self-defeating. (3) The opponent's argument is symmetric; if showing a miracle on a liar implies incapacity, then not showing it also implies incapacity, so no difference. (4) It is impossible for God to be incapable of creating a miracle after a liar's claim because splitting the moon is possible, and God is powerful over all possibles; there is no impediment in power or will since evil does not affect divine will. Thus the claim of impossibility is false.

Key Terms
معجز
تعجيز
دلالة
قدرة
إرادة
داعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A miracle on a liar is impossible because it would be inappropriate.
Correction: The author shows that it is not impossible in itself; only God's power and will determine its occurrence.

Checkpoint
In the fourth rebuttal, what example does the author use to show that a miracle on a liar is possible?
A) The splitting of the sea.
B) The splitting of the moon.
C) The resurrection of the dead.
D) The staff of Moses.

Key Takeaway
The third rebuttal shows symmetry, and the fourth proves that a miracle on a liar is intrinsically possible, defeating the opponent's objection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own life, have you ever assumed that because God can do something, He will do it for you? How does the fourth rebuttal challenge that assumption and call you to rely on His will rather than your expectations?
?
The third rebuttal shows that your own argument can be turned against you. Is there a belief you hold about religion that you have never questioned using the same standard you apply to others? Will you examine it today?
?
If God's motive is not affected by the 'ugliness' of a situation, what does that mean for how you view the trials in your life? Can you trust that His wisdom is greater than your sense of fairness, even when you don't understand?

Why Ash'ari View Undermines Prophethood
Argument that Ash'ari doctrine nullifies the basis for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari belief that God creates all human actions logically contradicts the rational basis for sending prophets.

Core Idea
Prophethood requires human capability; Ash'ari view denies it.

This passage presents a crisp rational argument against the Ash'ari position on human actions. The author shows that if God creates every human act, then humans are not truly responsible, making the prophetic call to obedience and avoidance of sin unreasonable. This is a key point in the debate on qadar and prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the logical structure: purpose of prophethood -> condition of capability -> consequence if denied.
The author uses a conditional argument: if X then Y, but Ash'arism implies not Y, so contradicting X.
2
Identify the main premise
What is the purpose of sending prophets according to the author? How does this purpose rely on human capability?
3
Understand 'obligating the incapable'
The author says the ugliness of obligating the incapable is known by primary intuition. Why is this a problem for the Ash'ari view?
This is a rational axiom: it is unjust to command someone who cannot obey.
4
Trace the logical conclusion
If the servant is not independent in action, then obligation becomes meaningless. Therefore, the Ash'ari view contradicts the affirmation of prophethood.
The argument is deductive: if P, then Q; but not Q, so not P.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني في بيان أن القول بأن الله تعالى خالق لأعمال العباد يمنع من القول بإثبات النبوات : وذلك لأن المقصود من بعثة الأنبياء عليهم السلام إلى الخلق دعوتهم إلى الطاعات ومنعهم عن القبائح والمنكرات . لكن دعوة الخلق إلى هذه الأشياء إنما تعقل عند كونهم قادرين على الأفعال لأن قبح تكليف العاجز معلوم في بدائه العقول . فإذا لم يكن العبد مستقلاً بالفعل والترك كان تكليفه تكليفاً للعاجز . فثبت أن القول بأن العبد غير موجد الأفعال نفسه ينافي الإقرار بالنبوة
The second point in explaining that the statement that God is the creator of the actions of servants prevents the statement of establishing prophethood: That is because the purpose of sending prophets, peace be upon them, to creation is to call them to obedience and prevent them from abominations and evil deeds. But calling creation to these things is only understood when they are capable of actions, because the ugliness of obligating the incapable is known in the primary intuitions of minds. So if the servant is not independent in action and omission, then his obligation is an obligation of the incapable. Thus it is established that the statement that the servant is not the creator of his own actions contradicts the affirmation of prophethood.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the Ash'ari view (God is creator of human actions) prevents establishing prophethood. The author states the purpose of sending prophets is to call people to obedience and forbid evil. This calling is meaningful only if humans are capable of actions; obligating the incapable is rationally impossible. If humans are not independent in action and omission (i.e., they do not create their own acts), then their obligation is like obligating an incapable person. Therefore, denying that humans are creators of their own actions contradicts the affirmation of prophethood, because it makes the prophetic call unreasonable.

Misconception: The Ash'ari view only affects human free will but does not impact prophethood.
Correction: This passage demonstrates that if humans do not create their actions, the prophetic call becomes irrational, thus directly contradicting the institution of prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why does the Ash'ari view contradict prophethood?
A) It denies God's power over actions.
B) It makes the prophetic call irrational by implying humans are incapable.
C) It rejects the need for prophets.
D) It claims prophets are not needed for guidance.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari doctrine that God is the sole creator of human actions makes the prophetic mission logically impossible because it undermines human capability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author argues that obligating the incapable is 'ugly in the primary intuitions of minds.' When you find yourself neglecting an obligation, do you treat it as a failure of your own capability or as a sign that Allah's command is somehow impossible? Which attitude aligns with the rational foundation of prophethood presented here?

Refuting the Objection on Miracles and Knowledge of Prophethood
Refutes the claim that miracles after false claims would prevent knowledge of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical rebuttal to the claim that miracles after false claims would prevent knowledge of prophethood.

Core Idea
Impossibility inherent in the evidence, not in God's power.

In this passage, the author tackles a tricky objection: if God could create a miracle after a liar's claim, wouldn't that make it impossible to know who is truthful? The author turns the argument on its head by distinguishing inherent impossibility from divine incapacity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the full English translation to get the gist of the argument.
Notice the dialectical structure: opponent's claim, author's response, then a counter-question.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and the author's response
The opponent claims that miracles after false claims would prevent knowledge of prophethood. The author responds by stating that it is necessary that God does not make us know through acquisition, otherwise it would imply incapacity. But the impossibility is inherent in the evidence itself.
The key move is turning the tables: the impossibility lies in the nature of the evidence, not in God's power.
3
Analyze the author's final comparison
The author asks why the opponent does not accept the same reasoning from someone who says the indication of miracle to truth is impossible in itself. There is no difference between the two sides.
This shows the opponent's objection is self-defeating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكاذب ، وإلا لزم تعجيزه على أن يعرفنا صدق الأنبياء بالاكتساب . ونحن نقول : وجب أن لا يصح من الله تعريفنا صدق الأنبياء بالاكتساب ، وإلا لزم تعجيزه عن خلق المعجزات ، عقيب دعوى الكذاب . ولما كان ممتنعاً في نفسه ، لم يكن عدم القدرة عليه عجزاً . قلنا : ولم ينفصلون عمن يقول : دلالة المعجز على الصدق ، لما كانت ممتنعة لنفسها ، لم يكن عدم القدرة على خلق هذا الدليل : عجزاً ؟ وبالجملة : فلا فرق بين الجانبين
The liar, otherwise it would necessitate incapacitating Him from making us know the truth of the prophets through acquisition. And we say: It is necessary that it is not valid for God to make us know the truth of the prophets through acquisition, otherwise it would necessitate incapacitating Him from creating miracles after the claim of the liar. And when it was impossible in itself, the lack of ability for it is not an incapacity. We said: And why do they not separate themselves from one who says: The indication of the miracle to truth, when it was impossible for itself, the lack of ability to create this evidence is not an incapacity? In summary: there is no difference between the two sides.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents a rebuttal to an objection concerning miracles and the knowledge of prophethood. It is a dialectical argument. The opponent claimed that if God could create a miracle after a liar's claim, then we could not know the truth of prophets through acquired miracles. The author responds by stating that it is necessary that God does not make us know the truth of prophets through acquisition, otherwise that would imply that God is incapable of creating miracles after a liar's claim. But since the impossibility (of the miracle after a liar) is inherent in the thing itself, the lack of ability to do it is not a sign of incapacity. The author then turns the argument back on the opponent: why don't they separate themselves from someone who says that the very indication of a miracle to truth is impossible in itself, so the lack of ability to create that evidence is not incapacity? So there is no difference between the two positions.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument shows that God cannot create miracles after liars.
Correction: The argument shows that the impossibility lies in the evidence itself, not in God's power.

Checkpoint

C) Miracles are impossible.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of a miracle after a false claim is inherent to the evidence, so it does not imply any incapacity in God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The argument here turns the opponent's logic back on them. Are there areas in your faith where you hold double standards—accepting one type of evidence while rejecting another without realizing the symmetry? What specific objection to Islamic teachings have you been holding that you need to re-examine in light of this principle?
?
This passage insists that the lack of ability to do something inherently impossible is not weakness. Reflect on a time you felt God was distant or not fulfilling a promise. Does that feeling stem from a misunderstanding of what is possible for God? How can this lesson reshape your expectations and reliance on His wisdom?

Rational Argument: Prophethood Requires Human Agency
Rational argument linking prophethood to human agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that the Ash'arite view of divine creation of actions negates the very purpose of prophethood.

Core Idea
Denying human agency makes prophetic calls meaningless.

The author presents a rational argument against the Ash'arite position that God creates all human actions. The purpose of sending prophets is to call people to obedience and forbid evil. This call only makes sense if people have the capacity to choose and act. If they are not independent agents, then imposing religious duties is like commanding an incapable person—an irrational act.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of argument.
Notice the logical structure: purpose → condition → absurdity → conclusion.
2
Identify the premise about prophethood
The author states that prophets are sent to call to obedience and prevent evil. Reflect on why this purpose is central.
3
Understand the innate moral principle
The author asserts that imposing duties on the incapable is known to be ugly by innate reason. This is a key rational axiom.
This axiom is accepted by all rational people.
4
Connect to the conclusion
If the servant is not independent in action, then religious duties become impositions on the incapable, which is absurd. Thus, denying human agency contradicts prophethood.
The conclusion is a direct logical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني في بيان أن القول بأن الله تعالى خالق لأعمال العباد ، يمنع من القول بإثبات النبوات : وذلك لأن المقصود من بعثة الأنبياء - عليهم السلام - إلى الخلق : دعوتهم إلى الطاعات، ومنعهم عن القبائح والمنكرات . لكن دعوة الخلق إلى هذه الأشياء إنما تعقل عند كونهم قادرين على الأفعال لأن قبح تكليف العاجز ، معلوم في بدائه العقول . فإذا لم يكن العبد مستقلاً بالفعل والترك ، كان تكليفه تكليفاً للعاجز . فثبت : أن القول بأن العبد غير موجد الأفعال نفسه ، ينافي الإقرار بالنبوة . الوجه الثالث : إن الكتب الإلهية بأسرها ناطقة بأن العباد قادرون على الخيرات والشرور متمكنون فيهما غير ممنوعين عنهما ، فمن شاء فليؤمن ، ومن شاء فليكفر ، وثبت بالمتواتر المقطوع به أنهم كانوا يمدحون من آمن وأطاع ، ويذمون من كفر وعصى . فلو قلنا : العبد غير مستقل بالفعل ، كان ذلك تصريحاً بكونهم ممنوعين من الأفعال، غير قادرين عليها . وذلك تصريح بتكذيب الأنبياء - عليهم السلام - في عين تلك الأشياء ، التي ادعوا كونهم رسل الله فيها . والتصريح بمثل هذا التكذيب ، ينافي الاعتراف بكونهم صادقين . فثبت بهذه الوجوه الثلاثة : أن القول بأن العبد غير موجد لأفعال نفسه ، ينافي الإقرار بالنبوة
The second aspect in explaining that the statement that God, exalted, is the creator of the actions of servants prevents the affirmation of prophethood: that is because the purpose of sending the prophets - peace be upon them - to creation is to call them to obedience and prevent them from ugly acts and wrongdoings. But calling creation to these things is only conceivable when they are capable of actions, because the ugliness of imposing a duty on the incapable is known in the primary intuitions of minds. So if the servant is not independent in action and omission, then imposing duties on him is imposing duties on the incapable. Thus it is established that the statement that the servant is not the originator of his own actions contradicts the acknowledgment of prophethood. The third aspect: Indeed, the divine books in their entirety state that the servants are capable of good and evil, are empowered in them, not prevented from them. 'So whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve' (Quran 18:29). And it is established by certain mass transmission that they used to praise those who believed and obeyed and blame those who disbelieved and disobeyed. So if we said that the servant is not independent in action, that would be a declaration that they are prevented from actions, not capable of them. And that is a declaration of disbelieving the prophets - peace be upon them - in the very things which they claimed to be messengers of God. And declaring such disavowal contradicts affirming that they are truthful. Thus it is established by these three aspects that the statement that the servant is not the originator of his own actions contradicts the acknowledgment of prophethood.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents two arguments (the second and third aspects) demonstrating that the Ash'arite view that God creates all human actions negates prophethood. The second argument is rational: the purpose of sending prophets is to call to obedience and forbid evil, but such a call only makes sense if people are capable of actions, because imposing duties on the incapable is morally repugnant and known by innate reason. If the servant is not independent in acting, then imposing duties is like imposing on an incapable person, which contradicts the very idea of prophethood. The third argument is scriptural: the divine books state that people are capable of good and evil, empowered, and not prevented. The Quran says 'whoever wills, let him believe...' and mass transmission shows that people were praised and blamed for their actions. If we deny that the servant is independent in action, we effectively declare that they are prevented from actions, which falsifies the prophets' message. Therefore, the view that the servant does not originate his own actions contradicts accepting prophethood.

Key Terms
خالق أعمال العباد
نبوات
تكليف
عاجز
استقلال بالفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because prophets cannot call incapable people.
B) Because imposing duties on the incapable is known to be ugly by innate reason.
C) Because the Quran says so.
D) Because God cannot command the incapable.

Key Takeaway
The rational argument shows that prophethood presupposes human agency; denying it undermines the whole purpose of sending prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The lesson says the ugliness of burdening the incapable is known by intuition. Do you live as if you are capable of obeying God? Or do you sometimes act as if you are a victim of your desires, denying your own agency? What would change if you fully owned your choices?

Scriptural Argument: Divine Books Affirm Human Choice
Scriptural argument using Quran and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural argument that the Quran and prophetic tradition affirm human capacity, contradicting the Ash'arite denial of independent action.

Core Idea
Scripture itself affirms that humans are capable and responsible.

The author now turns to scriptural evidence. The divine books, especially the Quran, clearly state that humans have the ability to choose good and evil. The Quran says 'whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve.' Furthermore, the consistent practice of praising the obedient and blaming the disobedient, transmitted by mass testimony, confirms human responsibility. If we deny that humans are independent in their actions, we would be denying the very messages the prophets brought.

Guided Path
1
Read the scriptural argument
Read the Arabic passage and translation, focusing on the evidence presented.
The argument uses Quran and sunna (praise/blame).
2
Examine the Quranic verse
Note the verse 'So whoever wills, let him believe...' What does it imply about human agency?
The verse implies a real choice.
3
Consider the role of praise and blame
The author mentions that by mass transmission, people were praised for good and blamed for evil. This confirms responsibility.
Mass transmission (tawatur) gives certainty.
4
Understand the implication of denial
If we say the servant is not independent, we are saying they are prevented, which contradicts the prophets' message, effectively accusing them of falsehood.
This would be a serious contradiction.
5
Grasp the final conclusion
The author concludes that denying human agency contradicts acknowledging prophethood, using the three aspects mentioned.
The conclusion ties back to the overall theme.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني في بيان أن القول بأن الله تعالى خالق لأعمال العباد ، يمنع من القول بإثبات النبوات : وذلك لأن المقصود من بعثة الأنبياء - عليهم السلام - إلى الخلق : دعوتهم إلى الطاعات، ومنعهم عن القبائح والمنكرات . لكن دعوة الخلق إلى هذه الأشياء إنما تعقل عند كونهم قادرين على الأفعال لأن قبح تكليف العاجز ، معلوم في بدائه العقول . فإذا لم يكن العبد مستقلاً بالفعل والترك ، كان تكليفه تكليفاً للعاجز . فثبت : أن القول بأن العبد غير موجد الأفعال نفسه ، ينافي الإقرار بالنبوة . الوجه الثالث : إن الكتب الإلهية بأسرها ناطقة بأن العباد قادرون على الخيرات والشرور متمكنون فيهما غير ممنوعين عنهما ، فمن شاء فليؤمن ، ومن شاء فليكفر ، وثبت بالمتواتر المقطوع به أنهم كانوا يمدحون من آمن وأطاع ، ويذمون من كفر وعصى . فلو قلنا : العبد غير مستقل بالفعل ، كان ذلك تصريحاً بكونهم ممنوعين من الأفعال، غير قادرين عليها . وذلك تصريح بتكذيب الأنبياء - عليهم السلام - في عين تلك الأشياء ، التي ادعوا كونهم رسل الله فيها . والتصريح بمثل هذا التكذيب ، ينافي الاعتراف بكونهم صادقين . فثبت بهذه الوجوه الثلاثة : أن القول بأن العبد غير موجد لأفعال نفسه ، ينافي الإقرار بالنبوة
The second aspect in explaining that the statement that God, exalted, is the creator of the actions of servants prevents the affirmation of prophethood: that is because the purpose of sending the prophets - peace be upon them - to creation is to call them to obedience and prevent them from ugly acts and wrongdoings. But calling creation to these things is only conceivable when they are capable of actions, because the ugliness of imposing a duty on the incapable is known in the primary intuitions of minds. So if the servant is not independent in action and omission, then imposing duties on him is imposing duties on the incapable. Thus it is established that the statement that the servant is not the originator of his own actions contradicts the acknowledgment of prophethood. The third aspect: Indeed, the divine books in their entirety state that the servants are capable of good and evil, are empowered in them, not prevented from them. 'So whoever wills, let him believe, and whoever wills, let him disbelieve' (Quran 18:29). And it is established by certain mass transmission that they used to praise those who believed and obeyed and blame those who disbelieved and disobeyed. So if we said that the servant is not independent in action, that would be a declaration that they are prevented from actions, not capable of them. And that is a declaration of disbelieving the prophets - peace be upon them - in the very things which they claimed to be messengers of God. And declaring such disavowal contradicts affirming that they are truthful. Thus it is established by these three aspects that the statement that the servant is not the originator of his own actions contradicts the acknowledgment of prophethood.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents two arguments (the second and third aspects) demonstrating that the Ash'arite view that God creates all human actions negates prophethood. The second argument is rational: the purpose of sending prophets is to call to obedience and forbid evil, but such a call only makes sense if people are capable of actions, because imposing duties on the incapable is morally repugnant and known by innate reason. If the servant is not independent in acting, then imposing duties is like imposing on an incapable person, which contradicts the very idea of prophethood. The third argument is scriptural: the divine books state that people are capable of good and evil, empowered, and not prevented. The Quran says 'whoever wills, let him believe...' and mass transmission shows that people were praised and blamed for their actions. If we deny that the servant is independent in action, we effectively declare that they are prevented from actions, which falsifies the prophets' message. Therefore, the view that the servant does not originate his own actions contradicts accepting prophethood.

Key Terms
كتب إلهية
متواتر
مدح
ذم
استقلال بالفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) God's absolute control over belief.
B) Human beings have the ability to choose belief or disbelief.
C) Prophets can choose to believe.
D) Only believers have free will.

Key Takeaway
Scripture and prophetic tradition consistently affirm human choice and responsibility, so denying human agency contradicts the prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
If you deny your own responsibility for your actions, then the commands of the prophets become hollow. Does your daily life reflect a belief that you are genuinely empowered to choose? Or do you live as if you are merely a victim of circumstances?
