The Determinist Response: Power Plus Motive
Determinist rebuts the tahaddi argument using the theory of power-plus-motive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how determinists respond to the tahaddi argument by attributing action to the combination of power and motive rather than human origination.

Core Idea
The ease of an action is due to a special quality, not human creative power.

After the tahaddi argument for human creative power, the determinist (mujbira) offers a response. They do not claim that humans have no power at all, but that the combination of power and motive can cause actions, and the difference between easy and hard actions is due to a special quality in the action itself. This lesson explores that response.

Guided Path
1
Read the determinist response
Read the passage where the determinist answers the objection. Notice that they accept that power + motive can cause some actions.
This is a concession to the opponent.
2
Understand the concept of power-plus-motive
The determinist argues that when power and motive combine, they may produce an action. If they don't, it's not because the agent didn't originate the action, but because the action lacks a special quality that would make it easy.
This preserves determinism by denying human origination.
3
Apply to the tahaddi context
In the case of the Quranic challenge, the Arabs had the power and the motive (to prove the Prophet wrong), but they could not produce the Quran. According to the determinist, this is because producing the Quran requires a special quality (mazid khususiyya) that was absent, so power+motive had no effect.
Thus, the challenge does not prove human creative power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال تعالى : ( وإن كنتم في ريب مما نزلنا على عبدنا . فأتووا بسورة من مثله ) إلى قوله : ( فإن لم تفعلوا ولن تفعلوا فاتقوا النار التي وقودها الناس والحجارة ) ووجه الاستدلال به : إن التحدي مع من يقدر على شيء من الأفعال . لأنه لما كان قادراً على الفعل في الجملة ، ثم عجز عن فعل له معنى خاص . دل ذلك على أن لذلك الفعل خصوصية. لأنه لو عجز ذلك الفاعل عن الإتيان بمسألة ، ولا يقدر على الفعل أصلا فإن التحدي معه لا يفيد الفائدة المطلوبة . إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إذا لم يكن العبد قادراً على الإيجاد والتكوين أصلاً ، لم يحصل التحدي بالقرآن على كونه معجزاً . ولما كان ذلك باطلاً بإجماع الأمة ، علمنا : أن العبد موجد . والجواب : إن هذا الإشكال غير وارد علينا . لانا سلمنا أن مجموع القدرة مع الداعي قد يوجب بعض الأفعال . وإذا لم يؤثرا في أمر من الأمور ، علمنا : أن ذلك المتيسر ممتاز عن ذلك المتعسر لمزيد خاصية ، لأجلها حصل ذلك اليسر .

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Determinists deny that humans have any power or role in actions.
Correction: Determinists acknowledge that humans have power (qudra) and motives (da'i), but they deny that humans independently originate actions. Actions result from the combination of power and motive, not from human creative power.

Checkpoint
According to the determinist response, what distinguishes an easy action from a difficult one?
A) The strength of the agent's will.
B) The agent's free choice.
C) An additional special quality in the easy action.
D) The amount of power available.

Key Takeaway
Determinists argue that the ease of certain actions is due to a special quality, not to human creative power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you struggle to do something you know is right, do you attribute that to a missing 'special quality' or to your own laziness? How does this lesson challenge your assumption that effort alone guarantees success?
?
If every easy action you perform is due to a quality not from you, what does that do to your pride in your achievements? Can you genuinely thank the One who grants that quality without feeling entitled?
?
This argument reduces your role as an originator of actions. Do you find that comforting or unsettling? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in Allah's absolute control over your deeds?
